b'Supported by'
b'By Shivani Vora'
b'Michael S. Meldman, 60, wasn\xe2\x80\x99t a golfer when he founded Discovery Land Company in 1994, a real estate business based in Scottsdale, Ariz., that has developed 25 private high-end golf communities in North America and the Caribbean.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMaster-planned communities and golf were hugely popular and the premium drivers in real estate,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 he said, \xe2\x80\x9cand I saw an opportunity, even though I hadn\xe2\x80\x99t ever really played golf. In fact, I only started playing seriously five years ago.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Today, Mr. Meldman\xe2\x80\x99s luxurious communities with members-only golf clubs \xe2\x80\x94 Baker\xe2\x80\x99s Bay in the Bahamas, Yellowstone Club in Big Sky, Mont., and Silo Ridge in Amenia, N.Y., among them \xe2\x80\x94 range from 450 acres to 14,000 acres, or about 180 hectares to 5,700 hectares, and have homes that command prices from $3 million to $80 million.'
b'The communities stand out for amenities that rival five-star destination resorts, with golf courses designed by Tom Fazio and Jack Nicklaus, restaurants with top-quality farm-to-table cuisine and an extensive range of wellness-themed activities. And let\xe2\x80\x99s not forget the Casamigos Tequila bar at each resort. (Mr. Meldman founded the brand with the entrepreneur Rande Gerber and the actor George Clooney.)'
b'Below are excerpts from a recent interview with Mr. Meldman.'
b'Tell me about your vision for Discovery Land Company.'
b'People were very interested in golf and master-planned communities, and my idea was to create a luxury concept that combined both. I wanted to find great pieces of land and build around the natural landscapes so that the communities looked like they belonged there, not like standard developments. They are all built to be sprawling with plenty of space between the homes and have lots of green space. And they all incorporate a lot of natural stone.'
b'Although the communities are in different locations, what characteristics do they share?'
b'They all have golf, of course. They\xe2\x80\x99re all gated and have guards, clubhouses with great gyms and spas and fantastic restaurants. They\xe2\x80\x99re also very family-friendly and casual. I think that a lot of golf clubs can be intimidating, but at ours, you can play barefoot in board shorts. And, we have two to three comfort stations on all the golf courses, which are basically mini-restaurants that serve everything from candy bars to foie gras to warm pretzels.'
b'In each resort, we hire locals to teach residents about the outdoor activities in the area. At Iron Horse in Whitefish, Mont., for example, you can go fly fishing. At Makena, in Maui, you can go deep sea fishing, scuba diving and snorkeling. And in most of our oceanside locations, kids can release baby turtles into the ocean. My idea is that the people who live in my communities should embrace the areas that they\xe2\x80\x99re in.'
b'How do you choose your locations?'
b'I seek out places where there is a good amount of land and where zoning allows us to build homes and a golf course. Also, there has to be enough to do in the area besides golf. In Silo Ridge, for example, in the Hudson Valley, which is the newest community, the horseback riding, hunting, mountain biking and hiking are all excellent.'
b'If you had to give one piece of advice for someone looking to buy a home in a golf community what would it be?'
b'Make sure that the developer has a track record of success and is going to commit to the vision of what they initially present.'
b'What are the most important features to get right when designing golf community homes?'
b'These days, I think they should have a more contemporary aesthetic as opposed to traditional, which was the norm when I started Discovery. They should have big windows that take advantage of the views, ideally of the golf course, and have spacious indoor and outdoor areas where families and friends can gather and spend time together like a nice-sized patio, a family room with comfortable, oversized couches and a dining room with a table that accommodates large groups. It\xe2\x80\x99s also great to have an open-plan home where the kitchen and family room are one big room, since these are the two areas where everyone tends to spend the most time. And the homes shouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be too close to each other so that everyone has enough privacy.'
b'In your opinion, how have golf communities changed over the last decade?'
b'They\xe2\x80\x99ve gone from golf being the only consideration to being simply one of many drivers. There is now a greater emphasis on cuisine, the nongolf outdoor pursuits and activities, the family-friendliness and the safety concerns addressed by being in a gated community.'
b'In a great golf community, there has to be something that\xe2\x80\x99s appealing to each family member. We have a lot of people living in our communities who don\xe2\x80\x99t golf. They\xe2\x80\x99re attracted to the other things Discovery clubs offer.'
b'Also, the demographic skews much younger. In the past, golf clubs attracted a lot of retirees, but now, there are a lot of people in their mid-30s to mid-40s enjoying them with their families that include young children.'
b'Are golf community residents different than your usual homeowner?'
b'I think that they\xe2\x80\x99re inherently more social. They\xe2\x80\x99re looking to connect with other people on a regular basis and love the idea of a sense of community. I\xe2\x80\x99m not saying other homeowners are antisocial, but they may not care as much about the social offerings and accessibility to the lineup of activities.'

b'Advertisement'
b'Supported by'
b'By Kevin Draper'
b'Through Tiger Woods\xe2\x80\x99s 11 years in the wilderness between major tournament wins, professional golf searched for a successor.'
b'Would it be Phil Mickelson, the once-snakebit lefty who is actually older than Woods but who got over the hump in 2004 to become his most formidable early-career challenger? How about Rory McIlroy, the phenom from Northern Ireland, whose brutal collapse in the final round of the 2011 Masters was immediately followed by his first major championship? Or maybe Jordan Spieth, whose Masters win in 2015 tied Woods for the 72-hole record?'
b'Ultimately, it ended up being all of them, and therefore none of them. Each had a handful of major tournament wins and at times looked as if he could dominate the sport. But none emerged as the next Tiger. Golf itself stagnated as Woods struggled, his shadow looming in a way that was almost as impactful as his presence had been for the previous decade.'
b'Now that Woods is back on top, the question is whether the sport can take advantage of his twilight years to build something that survives when his career finally does end.'
b'Jay Monahan, the commissioner of the PGA Tour, believes the sport is well positioned to capitalize on the re-emergence of Woods. He pointed to the new schedule, with the P.G.A. Championship held in May, and a long-term, $2 billion international television rights agreement with Discovery.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not like you change your business in a moment like this,\xe2\x80\x9d Monahan said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou think about how you get to a moment like this and put your tour and product in the best possible position.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'By most metrics, golf peaked in the early 2000s, at the height of the first Tigermania. According to Gallup, in 2000, 5 percent of Americans surveyed said golf was their favorite sport to watch. By 2017, that number was 1 percent. Golf was tied with volleyball, boxing, gymnastics, motocross, figure skating and rodeo.'
b'According to the Sports and Fitness Industry Association, 29.5 million Americans played a round of golf in 2007. In 2017, that number was 23.8 million, a decline of 19.3 percent.'
b'Unlike most other sports, which believe fans respond most to parity, Woods\xe2\x80\x99s dominance was electrifying for golf. From June 1997 \xe2\x80\x94 when he first became the world\xe2\x80\x99s No. 1-ranked golfer \xe2\x80\x94 to October 2010, only four golfers besides Woods were ranked No. 1, for a total of less than a year and a half. Woods was ranked first for two different five-year streaks in that time.'
b'Since October 2010, 11 golfers have been ranked No. 1, and only committed golf fans and golfers can name more than a few of them.'
b'The money available to golf professionals, however, continues to grow, and if Woods keeps winning he\xe2\x80\x99ll do something few athletes get to: Profit from the explosive growth in revenue that the athlete himself drove.'
b'In professional sports, athletes benefit from the stars of the preceding generation driving interest. Magic Johnson earned less than $24 million in his entire career; LeBron James earned $33 million this season.'
b'In 2019, the top prize at each tournament on the PGA Tour \xe2\x80\x94 even the Corales Puntacana Resort and Club Championship \xe2\x80\x94 is more than Woods earned for winning the 1997 Masters. The FedEx Cup bonus pool has doubled, to $70 million.'
b'The massive growth in professional golf\xe2\x80\x99s revenue over the past two decades isn\xe2\x80\x99t due solely to Woods, but he was certainly its biggest driver. In the nearly 11 years between major wins for Woods, in which he was revealed to be a serial adulterer, pleaded guilty to reckless driving, had four back surgeries and didn\xe2\x80\x99t even enter a major for two years, numerous segments of the business of golf struggled.'
b'Nike, the company that has paid Woods hundreds of millions of dollars and whose red shirts he religiously wears on tournament Sundays, dived into the business when Woods turned pro in 1996 and signed him to an apparel endorsement contract. At the time, Nike manufactured only a limited selection of golf clothing, not equipment.'
b'Three years later, Nike began manufacturing golf balls, and three years after that, golf clubs. Woods, who had used Titleist clubs, started using Nike equipment. But as Nike\xe2\x80\x99s golf business crested with the Tiger wave, it too crashed amid Woods\xe2\x80\x99s down years.'
b'Revenue in Nike\xe2\x80\x99s golf division peaked in 2013 \xe2\x80\x94 the year Woods had two top-10 finishes at majors and looked to have gotten his career back on track, until he either missed the cut or did not enter 15 of the next 18 majors. In 2016, the company announced it was exiting the golf equipment market. Around the same time, Adidas sold off its money-losing TaylorMade golf division.'
b'Tim Derdenger, a professor of marketing and strategy at Carnegie Mellon\xe2\x80\x99s business school and a scratch golfer who has written numerous papers on Woods and celebrity endorsements, said the golf world could learn a great deal from how consumers and golfers reacted to Woods.'
b'As an endorser who at one point was collecting some $50 million a year in sponsorship deals, Woods had what marketing experts call a \xe2\x80\x9cgolden halo effect,\xe2\x80\x9d Derdenger said. Initially, people wanted to buy products associated with Woods because they aspired to identify with him. Those deals largely went away after Woods\xe2\x80\x99s sordid 2009, but if the halo effect returns, so will the sponsorships.'
b'Derdenger said Woods also provided \xe2\x80\x9cinformational value\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 people believed the apparel and equipment he endorsed was of high quality, as long as he was high in the world golf rankings.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere was still value in Nike retaining Tiger Woods because of this extra endorsement effect that wasn\xe2\x80\x99t eroded from the scandal,\xe2\x80\x9d Derdenger said.'
b'Woods has a similar effect on the tournaments he enters. When he is competing and on the leaderboard, fans view it as a quality event worthy of their attention. Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s television ratings were the highest for the third round of a tournament since 2015, and Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s viewership was solid considering start times were moved up hours to accommodate inclement weather.'
b'Whether those viewers included minorities who will become golfers, as so many predicted in the late 1990s, is another question. According to the National Golf Foundation, minorities in 2017 made up 18 percent of all United States golfers, while they made up 25 percent of new golfers. Two decades ago, just 6 percent of new golfers were minorities.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere is more diversity in the game than there was 10 years ago,\xe2\x80\x9d said Pete Bevacqua, the president of the NBC Sports Group and a former chief executive of the PGA of America. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think those numbers are good enough yet, but golf is aware of it and trying to make it better.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Less clear is whether these people end up sticking with the sport, and whether they have the means to sustain their initial interest. Professional golf is incrementally more diverse than when Woods started, but there hasn\xe2\x80\x99t been a wholesale influx of African-Americans or otherwise non-Caucasians into the sport at either the amateur or professional level.'
b'Monahan, who took charge of the PGA Tour in 2017, said growing and diversifying golf\xe2\x80\x99s fan base were his top priorities. That is achieved through getting people to try nontraditional versions of golf, like Topgolf and video game golf, and providing viewers myriad options to watch.'
b'It also means getting children to play through the First Tee, a youth development organization formed in 1997, or Woods\xe2\x80\x99s TGR foundation. Monahan is hopeful Woods\xe2\x80\x99s win will be galvanizing. \xe2\x80\x9cThese moments bring more people into our sport,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'By Karen Crouse'
b'RANCHO MIRAGE, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 Ally McDonald started the weekend as the highest L.P.G.A. nonwinner on the ANA Inspiration leaderboard. Could she become the second consecutive player, after Pernille Lindberg, to make the year\xe2\x80\x99s first major her first L.P.G.A. victory?'
b'Back in Mississippi, her home state, the players who competed against McDonald in high school know better than to discount her chances. After she took the first-round lead, two men posted recollections on the L.P.G.A.\xe2\x80\x99s Facebook page of being outclassed by McDonald, who won the boys\xe2\x80\x99 state championship in her senior year at Itawamba Agricultural High School.'
b'McDonald, 26, competed on the boys\xe2\x80\x99 team because there wasn\xe2\x80\x99t enough interest to field a girls\xe2\x80\x99 squad. \xe2\x80\x9cOnce I got to probably my freshman, sophomore year, the state changed regulations and I had to move back to the boys\xe2\x80\x99 tees,\xe2\x80\x9d McDonald said on Friday, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cThey said if I was going to play with the boys, then you\xe2\x80\x99re going to have to play where the boys play from.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'McDonald, who carded a two-over 74 on Saturday and is six strokes behind the leader, Jin Young Ko, recalled winning the state title on a course that was longer than Mission Hills Country Club\xe2\x80\x99s 6,834-yard layout, and in their Facebook posts, Peyton Dunlap and Chandler Thompson remembered her \xe2\x80\x9cwhipping up\xe2\x80\x9d on them. There were a few exceptions, said McDonald, who went on to star at Mississippi State, \xe2\x80\x9cbut as a whole, the guys that I was surrounded by always respected me.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'On the L.P.G.A. Tour, the women are playing for more than money, trophies and world-ranking points. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat we\xe2\x80\x99re working toward is having the same amount of respect that the men get,\xe2\x80\x9d said Jessica Korda, the women\xe2\x80\x99s world No. 11.'
b'Korda, who is in a group tied for eighth with, among others, McDonald after a third-round 71, is the women\xe2\x80\x99s leader in the inaugural Aon Risk Reward Challenge, a competition on the PGA and L.P.G.A. Tours featuring a running tally of players\xe2\x80\x99 scores on designated holes. At the end of the season, the players on each tour with the lowest scores in relation to par will receive $1 million bonuses.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a great step in the right direction,\xe2\x80\x9d Korda said, referring to the equal prize money.'
b'The Tuesday before the first round of the ANA Inspiration was Equal Pay Day, the point in 2019 that women had to work until to earn what men made in 2018. In golf, the gender pay disparity is glaring.'
b'When Georgia Hall won the Women\xe2\x80\x99s British Open at Royal Lytham last August, she earned $490,000. A month earlier, Francesco Molinari collected $1.89 million for his victory at the men\xe2\x80\x99s British Open at Carnoustie.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s not only golf, clearly, it\xe2\x80\x99s society, and we need to aim for having the same opportunities and the same prize fund in this eventually,\xe2\x80\x9d Molinari said last month.'
b'Molinari has spent time around Hall at events for AON, a global professional services firm that uses both as brand ambassadors. Like McDonald\xe2\x80\x99s male high school teammates, Molinari has more respect for Hall after getting to know her.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe main thing is when you meet women like that, you see in the end we do the same thing, we have the same drive, the same passion, the same dreams,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cEverything is exactly the same.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The onus is not on the women to narrow the gap, he added, but on their male peers and on those who control the corporate coffers.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat we can do as players is support the ladies\xe2\x80\x99 tour,\xe2\x80\x9d Molinari said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut I think the main thing is the exposure they get. It\xe2\x80\x99s nowhere near where it should be, and that creates less interest in sponsors, less money.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Molinari\xe2\x80\x99s words rang as true as bird song Saturday as the best women in the world took a back seat to the top up-and-coming women, whose final round of the Augusta National Women\xe2\x80\x99s Amateur, played on the same course that will host next week\xe2\x80\x99s Masters, was shown on NBC. The three hours of network coverage bestowed upon the likes of the winner, the women\xe2\x80\x99s world No. 1 amateur, Jennifer Kupcho, and the runner-up, Maria Fassi of Mexico, was three hours more than was conferred on McDonald, Korda, Hall and Company at the ANA Inspiration.'
b'To Molinari\xe2\x80\x99s point, neither Bank of America nor AT&T, two of the corporate sponsors whose girl-power-themed ads were in heavy rotation during Saturday\xe2\x80\x99s Augusta women\xe2\x80\x99s amateur final-round coverage, sponsors an L.P.G.A. event.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI think all we can do is try to play the best golf we can and show the public and the sponsors and the media what we can do,\xe2\x80\x9d Hall said.'
b'On this great week for women\xe2\x80\x99s golf, is it progress that the Augusta National Women\xe2\x80\x99s Amateur runner-up had a bigger stage and audience than the reigning Women\xe2\x80\x99s British Open winner?'
b'On the eve of the ANA Inspiration, which started on Thursday, the L.P.G.A. commissioner, Mike Whan, told reporters: \xe2\x80\x9cIn my mind, the Augusta Women\xe2\x80\x99s Amateur is an evolution, not a revolution. But maybe in time, it will be the revolution that I want it to be.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Pavlos Zafiropoulos'
b'PYLOS, Greece \xe2\x80\x94 On the southwestern Peloponnese coast of Greece, in walking distance from the beach, Thodoris Poulis, a construction foreman, pointed up recently at half a dozen newly built homes on the hillside, each with a sweeping view of the Bay of Navarino.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe older sort of development with a few small houses is going away,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cand we\xe2\x80\x99re getting more large stand-alone homes \xe2\x80\x94 expensive builds, in the style of villas.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As he spoke, he was overseeing work on what will become just such a villa; dubbed the Lemon Project, this home near the town of Pylos will have a pool, a sea view and landscaped gardens, complete with citrus orchard.'
b'The developer of that property, Iliopoulos Real Estate and Constructions, is a small family business run by two brothers, Minas and Vasilis Iliopoulos. Until recently, their business usually involved building or renovating modest homes on plots owned by others here in the Messenia region.'
b'But with the Lemon Project, they have become developers, buying the land themselves and building a luxury home that they will put on the market for about 800,000 euros, or about $900,000.'
b'Part of the reason they can do this can be found in a very different construction site only a short distance away.'
b'In the hills above Pylos, large machines crack and pulverize boulders clawed from the ground.'
b'Dwarfed by rising slopes on either side, they are carving out what will become an artificial lake \xe2\x80\x94 an irrigation reservoir for two new 18-hole golf courses. When completed in 2021, the courses will unfold over 370 acres across the hilltops and provide golfers with sweeping views of the olive groves and the sea below.'
b'These courses, designed by the two-time Masters champion Jos\xc3\xa9 Mar\xc3\xada Olaz\xc3\xa1bal and christened Navarino Hills by the developer, Temes, are a major undertaking by any standard. Yet they are only the latest project on which the company has broken ground in a multifaceted effort to remake this onetime sleepy region into a world-renowned golf and holiday destination under the brand Costa Navarino.'
b'Alongside its flagship Navarino Dunes resort, with its two five-star hotels, extensive spa and myriad other amenities, Temes has already built two other 18-hole signature golf courses in the area: The Dunes Course, which opened with the resort in 2010, and The Bay Course, opened in 2011 and just below Navarino Hills.'
b'They are responding to what has become a truism in the golf course business. \xe2\x80\x9cWith golf courses there is the following issue: One equals almost none,\xe2\x80\x9d said Achilles Constantakopoulos, the chairman of Temes. He cited a survey by the International Association of Golf Tour Operators that found that only 15 percent of dedicated golfers would consider visiting a new destination with just one golf course. That figure rises to 75 percent with three golf courses and to 100 percent with five.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s important is not just to have a golf course, but to be considered a golf destination,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Constantakopoulos said, \xe2\x80\x9cthen it becomes a decision-making factor.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ambitious as it may be, turning Messenia into a place that lures high-spending golfers away from other more established destinations is just one aspect of the company\xe2\x80\x99s multipronged strategy. It is one that seeks to not only increase tourism to Messenia, but to do so year-round \xe2\x80\x94 an almost unheard-of goal in a country where the overwhelming majority of visitors arrive between June and September. Golf serves that purpose, by providing a reason to visit outside the summer months.'
b'Another key aim is for some of the newly acquired visitors to purchase homes, becoming regular contributors to the local economy for years to come.'
b'That strategy appears to be bearing fruit beyond the carefully manicured grounds of Costa Navarino.'
b'In the Iliopoulos brothers\xe2\x80\x99 office in Pylos, lined with images of properties for sale, a cluster of golf clubs stands in a corner. On the shelf above it sits a glass container half filled with golf balls printed with the company\xe2\x80\x99s logo. Neither of the brothers plays golf.'
b'Putting up a development like the Lemon Project would have been unthinkable only a few years ago; in 2013, thanks to the uncertainty swirling around Greece\xe2\x80\x99s fiscal crisis and with domestic bank lending effectively nonexistent, the construction business in the Messenia area had ground almost to a halt. But things soon turned around.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cSince 2016 we have been on an upward trajectory,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 said Minas Iliopoulos. \xe2\x80\x9cWe have been growing every year. And tourism is on the rise. Quality tourism.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The brothers\xe2\x80\x99 optimism does not appear to be unfounded. Savills Greece, a real estate agency, said in a statement that \xe2\x80\x9cthe second home market in Messenia has changed drastically in the last 10 years.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cInterest for a second home in the area has significantly risen,\xe2\x80\x9d the agency said, \xe2\x80\x9cand thus prices have also gone up, since owners see continued demand.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'According to Savills Greece, average prices for second homes in Messenia are generally between \xe2\x82\xac230 and \xe2\x82\xac325 per square foot, with prices exceeding \xe2\x82\xac465 per square foot for \xe2\x80\x9cvery special properties.\xe2\x80\x9d While Savills notes that in many cases sellers\xe2\x80\x99 initial asking prices are overly optimistic, \xe2\x80\x9cabove average prices have shown significant growth in the last decade.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Temes\xe2\x80\x99s grand plan to remake the region is one that has been decades in the making, essentially the vision of Vassilis Constantakopoulos, Achilles Constantakopoulos\xe2\x80\x99s father and the founder of Temes. He died in 2011, but is still referred to as the Captain by many Temes employees and Messenians alike.'
b'Born to a poor family in the Messenian village of Diavolitsi, Vassilis Constantakopoulos left his homeland for Athens during the 1946-49 Greek Civil War at around 13 years of age.'
b'By the mid-1970s he had founded the shipping company Costamare, through which he amassed a great fortune. In the 1980s he began regularly visiting his homeland and buying land piecemeal, laying the groundwork for what would become today\xe2\x80\x99s Costa Navarino.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHis vision was to create a new tourism destination in the Mediterranean and in parallel to give work to the people, so they wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t need to leave as he had left at 12, 13 years old,\xe2\x80\x9d Achilles Constantakopoulos said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe had a very strong feeling for the people of the area. And he saw that Messenia as an area had great potential for tourism which was not being realized.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the meantime, one of the most significant obstacles to tourism in the region \xe2\x80\x94 its historically poor transportation links \xe2\x80\x94 has been largely overcome.'
b'Once a five-hour journey along winding country roads, the completion of a major infrastructure project has turned the drive from Athens into a two-and-a-half hour trip along a highway that slices through the mountainous landscape via tunnels and bridges.'
b'And the airport of the city Kalamata, 45 minutes from Pylos, now receives more than 1,300 international flights a year \xe2\x80\x94 up 450 percent from a decade ago \xe2\x80\x94 in part because Temes has spent millions to woo international carriers. In 2012 the airport was renamed the Captain Vassilis Constantakopoulos Kalamata International Airport.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cMessenia is one of the few destinations in Europe which is at once easily accessible but unspoiled,\xe2\x80\x9d Achilles Constantakopoulos said. \xe2\x80\x9cThis combination is very rare.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'With Messenia now on the international tourism map, in 2017 Temes rolled out another key stage of its plan: offering upscale holiday homes for purchase.'
b'The Navarino Residences were the first to go on the market. The luxury villas, located at Navarino Dunes, are fully customizable, have a minimum floor space of 4,300 square feet and a starting price of \xe2\x82\xac2.4 million. Of the 30 initially offered, 18 have been purchased. Another 20 will be offered at a later date.'
b'Their architectural design is based in part on a 19th-century building preserved on the Costa Navarino grounds, which was recently renovated to become a luxury villa.'
b'Navarino Residences were followed in 2018 by Navarino Apartments. At the lower end of the company\xe2\x80\x99s planned real estate offerings, these 1,300-square-foot units have a starting price just under \xe2\x82\xac500,000.'
b'In both cases, buyers get multiple benefits from owning a property integrated into the resort, including free access to the complex\xe2\x80\x99s amenities and rent-sharing programs that will generate profit when they are away.'
b'Yet even with the interest that Costa Navarino has generated, second-home prices in the immediate vicinity of the resort remain significantly below those in more established Greek holiday destinations such as the Cyclades or Corfu. In these areas, according to Savills, average prices for holiday homes are about \xe2\x82\xac370 per square foot; luxury homes go for above \xe2\x82\xac740 per square foot.'
b'And further afield, around Kalamata and toward the eastern boundary of Messenia near the Mani Peninsula, many properties remain accessible to buyers of even modest means.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere are excellent opportunities anywhere in the Messenian Peloponnese,\xe2\x80\x9d said Mary O\xe2\x80\x99Connor, who for 20 years has run a real estate business in Kalamata with her husband, specializing in the second-home market. \xe2\x80\x9cExcept for around Pylos,\xe2\x80\x9d she added, where properties have become scarce. But even there, she said, \xe2\x80\x9cthere are a few good plots left.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99'
b'In other areas and villages, Ms. O\xe2\x80\x99Connor said, plots and fixer-upper houses can still be bought for prices below \xe2\x82\xac50,000.'
b'George Elliott, 67, bought a fixer-upper in Messenia in 2001 and now lives there about six months a year. His house was once the village\xe2\x80\x99s olive press. (The basement still has lots of the original machinery.) He is grateful that the Costa Navarino development has helped bring decent transportation to the area.'
b'He would happily play golf, too. But he plays only in London, where he said it costs about $17. The Costa Navarino golf courses are just too expensive for him. \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t have that kind of pension,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'By The Associated Press'
b'AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 Bryson DeChambeau seemed about as excited as a mad scientist gets as Masters week kicked off, which meant he stopped just short of jumping for joy.'
b"Not to worry. The jump might come Sunday for DeChambeau, assuming the planets align, the morning dew on the golf ball is at proper levels and putts don't bounce off the flagstick."
b'If not, well, all bets are off.'
b"Golf's most noted iconoclast \xe2\x80\x94 the only one in the field with irons that are all the same length \xe2\x80\x94 tees off in his third Masters not only with visions of a green jacket but a legitimate chance of being in the mix late Sunday afternoon."
b'And why not? DeChambeau has won five times in the past year, rising from 62nd in the world golf rankings to sixth while building a reputation as both a crafty calculator and steely closer.'
b"Not only that, he discovered something last week \xe2\x80\x94 just what he won't say \xe2\x80\x94 that might make him just as effective with his short wedges as he has been with the rest of his game."
b'"I\'ve had some disadvantages with a couple of the irons I\'ve had for a little bit," DeChambeau said. "And just being able to practice and getting comfortable and seeing the ball flights come out the proper way for the first time ever in my life is pretty cool."'
b"That's DeChambeau. Always tweaking, always studying."
b"He's called the mad scientist for a reason. DeChambeau's swing is a study in the science of single plane, he plays irons that are all the same length so everything can be repeatable, and he studies contours in greens like they were clues to where the late union leader Jimmy Hoffa is buried."
b"What he would like to be called is Masters champion. And that's why he was working last week with new wedges \xe2\x80\x94 still the same length as his other irons \xe2\x80\x94 in search of a breakthrough that might trim a shot or two off at Augusta National."
b'"I\'ve been fortunate to win a lot of tournaments using the equipment that I\'ve had so far and it\'s been great," DeChambeau said. "But there\'s always that little bit of room for improvement. So we\'ve been working quite heavily this past week in trying to figure out some things that could give me an advantage this week."'
b"What may not be an advantage for DeChambeau is that there's no green mapping book for players at the Masters. Instead of staring at diagrams of contours on a green to see how a putt breaks, he'll have to rely on looking at the contours themselves."
b"But he's got a plan for that, too, just like he has a plan for most things in his golf career."
b'"I have to practice a lot more hitting breaking putts because I can\'t just bring out my compass and go, oh, it\'s 3 percent and here it is," DeChambeau said. "I have to look at and walk around and go, \'OK, I\'m acclimated to 3 percent.\'"'
b"If the calculations are all a bit too much to understand, don't worry. Arnold Palmer would have been confused, too, and he won four green jackets."
b'Technology, though, is the new wave in golf, and DeChambeau is its leader in the clubhouse. He uses words in conversation that are heard more often in physics classes than golf courses and talks about scientific advances in golf like other players might be discussing the latest in movies.'
b"That includes spending more time than usual this week figuring out exactly what moisture on the clubface will do at Augusta National, where rain is forecast during the week. To make sure he's doing it right, DeChambeau sprays balls on the practice range with salt water to see how they react."
b'"That\'s going to affect the way the ball reacts on the face," he said. "You know, there\'s a percentage to that, and we have to account for that. If you don\'t, you\'re going to hit it to 30, 40 feet, instead of 10 feet."'
b"It may be too much information for casual golf fans, or even many of DeChambeau's fellow pros. No one else has really embraced his thoughts on swing plane and single length irons, but DeChambeau says he hopes some children taking up the game try and adopt it."
b'For now, the 25-year-old is focused on his wedges and the greens at Augusta National. He first came here as an amateur in 2016 and thought he had a chance at winning before hitting it into the bushes on 18 on his second day, and only broke par one round last year before finishing in a tie for 38th.'
b'Whatever happens, one thing is for sure.'
b"If DeChambeau doesn't win, he can't just blame it on bad luck."

b'By Reuters'
b"(Reuters) - Tiger Woods' victory at the Masters golf tournament on Sunday, his first major victory since 2008, is expected to lift sales for sponsors, broadcasters and golf courses lucky enough to host a tournament with Woods playing."
b'The competition put the 43-year-old back on top of a sport he helped transform 25 years ago. '
b'"Tiger sells golf," says Eric Smallwood, president of Apex Marketing Group, Inc., a Michigan analytics firm. Apex found that Nike earned $22.5 million worth of brand exposure just from Woods\xe2\x80\x99 final round, with Nike\xe2\x80\x99s "Swoosh" logo splashed on his hat, shirt, pants and shoes. Nike stock was up about one percent on Monday. '
b"Tournament broadcaster CBS Corp saw a ratings bump. Based on preliminary data, the final round of Sunday's tournament was the highest-rated morning golf broadcast since 1986, when CBS started collecting that data. The tournament, which is usually broadcast in the afternoon, was rescheduled to the morning because of weather."
b"CBS has the rights to the PGA Championship in May and expects prices for advertising time that is still available to rise as a result of Woods' Masters victory, according to a source familiar with the matter."
b'The golf demographic is wealthier and better-educated than other sports fans, so TV ratings are valued more highly because they\xe2\x80\x99re more apt to turn into sales, even of big-ticket items, said Neal Pilson, president of Pilson Communications and former president of CBS Sports. '
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHistorically, events where Tiger Woods is on leaderboards on Sunday generated 30 to 40 percent higher ratings in the United States for those tournaments,\xe2\x80\x9d Pilson said. '
b'MAKINGS OF A COMEBACK'
b'Woods was a 20-year-old prodigy when he turned pro in 1996. Less than a year later he was ranked No. 1 in the world. He struck lucrative endorsement deals - including a five-year, $40 million deal with Nike - and golf experienced a surge in popularity. '
b"Then Woods' personal life collapsed and with it, his brand. In 2009, after the news of multiple infidelities, he lost endorsement deals with companies like AT&T Inc and Accenture Plc. Other sponsors, such as Procter & Gamble Co's Gillette and Berkshire Hathaway Inc's NetJets, kept their contracts with Woods but stopped using him in marketing. "
b'Four back surgeries later, Woods continued to suffer professionally and in the public eye. In 2017 police arrested him for driving under the influence; he pleaded guilty to reckless driving and entered a program for first-time offenders. '
b'In 2018 Woods began a professional comeback that culminated at Sunday\'s Masters. After his victory, Nike, which stood behind Woods throughout his darker years, posted an ad on its website titled \xe2\x80\x9cTiger Woods: Same Dream."'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn sports you have heroes, villains and underdogs," said Benjamin Hordell, founder of digital marketing and advertising firm DXagency. "Tiger has lived all of it. That\xe2\x80\x99s amazing from a storytelling perspective. People will root against him, but they\xe2\x80\x99re watching." '
b'On Monday U.S. President Donald Trump said he would award Woods the Presidential Medal of Freedom. '
b' (Reporting by Helen Coster and Hilary Russ. Additional reporting by Sheila Dang. Editing by Kenneth Li and Cynthia Osterman)'

b'By Shivani Vora'
b'It is a buyer\xe2\x80\x99s market for consumers interested in buying property in a golf community, whether a hotel resort with residences or a residential-only development.'
b'Gregory Nathan, the chief business officer for the National Golf Foundation, a golf market research provider, said that a building boom from 1986 to 2006 produced a flood of homes at top-quality golf courses, mostly in the United States but internationally, too.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThere is still plenty of supply to spare, and the competition among golf communities to woo buyers is fierce,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'While interest in golf community homes waned after the 2008 recession, that is no longer the case, said Gregory Daco, the chief United States economist for Oxford Economics USA.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe global economy is stronger, and people have more disposable income to spare, which means that they\xe2\x80\x99re more apt to invest in secondary purchases like golf homes,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'But before buyers decide to live in such a community, they should consider several factors. Here is advice on how to make an informed decision about buying a golf home:'
b''
b'IT\xe2\x80\x99S ALL ABOUT THE LOCATION'
b'First and foremost, even before looking at prospective properties, consider the destinations.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou should like the idea of living where you\xe2\x80\x99re looking,\xe2\x80\x9d said Patrick Melton, a co-founder and managing partner of South Street Partners, a private equity real estate investment firm based in Charlotte, N.C., and Charleston, S.C. The firm owns Kiawah Island Club, a golf community near Charleston with residences and two golf courses.'
b'If you\xe2\x80\x99ve spent time in and enjoy Miami or Spain\xe2\x80\x99s Costa del Sol region, both of which have an abundance of golf communities, for example, seek out homes in these areas. On the flip side, if you\xe2\x80\x99re enamored of countryside golf communities but don\xe2\x80\x99t particularly like being in remote settings, look for a site that\xe2\x80\x99s in a suburb and close to a city.'
b'Many consumers fall in love with a golf community and buy a home there, Mr. Melton said, only to realize afterward that they\xe2\x80\x99re not thrilled with the area.'
b'Also, consider whether being near quality medical care, an international airport, noteworthy restaurants and an arts and culture scene is a priority.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYour home could tick all the boxes in terms of what you\xe2\x80\x99re looking for, but it may be an hour\xe2\x80\x99s drive to a major grocery store or hospital, which could be a hassle,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Melton said.'
b'And don\xe2\x80\x99t forget about the weather. Some destinations are too cold to play golf or spend time outdoors in winter or may have a rainy or hurricane season, while others are almost too hot in summer, said Liz Rowlinson, editor of A Place in the Sun magazine, a division of the British-based real-estate consulting brand of the same name.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you want to play golf year-round and want a home that\xe2\x80\x99s appealing to be in year-round, you should look for a property located in a region with a stable climate, save for maybe a few months,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'But location also means the exact position of your home, Ms. Rowlinson said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLiving right next to a green or fairway sounds idyllic but early morning mowers can be noisy, sprinklers come on during the night, and fast-moving golf balls landing in your pool is tiresome,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'The bottom line is that if you\xe2\x80\x99re sensitive to noise, the crack of tee shot drives is far louder than the murmur of greenside putts.'
b'Similarly, you may like views across fairways, but will you be happy with golfers staring into your home as they pass by? A strategically placed line of bushes can provide privacy.'
b'If you\xe2\x80\x99re an avid golfer, the number of other good courses nearby should figure in, too; playing at your own club week after week may get dull.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIdeally, you\xe2\x80\x99d want at least a few public courses less than an hour\xe2\x80\x99s drive from you, so you have the option for some variety when you play,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Rowlinson said.'
b''
b'FIND AN EXPERIENCED BROKER'
b'More often than not, buyers interested in golf communities usually don\xe2\x80\x99t work with brokers who are well informed about the areas they\xe2\x80\x99re looking in, said Blake Plumley, the chief executive of Capital Pursuits, a development consulting firm specializing in resort residential communities. When interviewing potential brokers, ask them how many properties they have sold in the communities. Ideally, it should be several.'
b'Also, inquire about three positive aspects and three drawbacks of living in those communities. \xe2\x80\x9cYour broker should be able to easily answer this,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Plumley said.'
b'The broker should personally know the golf club\xe2\x80\x99s membership director, the general manager, the head golf pro and a few other key figures in the communities. \xe2\x80\x9cYou want a broker who can directly introduce you to these people,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Plumley said.'
b''
b'LOOK FOR KEY AMENITIES'
b'Successful golf communities offer much more than golf \xe2\x80\x94 so much that they most likely attract plenty of nongolfing residents, Ms. Rowlinson said.'
b'Desirable amenities include a clubhouse with more than one social gathering space, tennis courts, an outdoor pool with a grill area, a high-quality restaurant, a casual dining option and a bar. A family-friendly club is also important. The best communities have a robust lineup of activities for children and families, such as summer camps, boating and hiking excursions, pool days, fun food-themed dinners such as taco night and more.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe more amenities a community has, the broader its appeal is, making your home more sellable if you ever look to move,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Melton said.'
b''
b'UNDERSTAND FINANCIAL COMMITMENTS'
b'Living in a golf development comes with additional costs that could include club dues, property taxes and monthly maintenance fees. These costs can vary greatly from one community to the next, and while the home you are considering might be affordable, the price of living in the community could be exorbitant.'
b'Also, some communities assess their residents, while others don\xe2\x80\x99t. That means that residents are billed for the cost of projects such as a new health club or repairing the clubhouse\xe2\x80\x99s leaky roof. Financially sound communities have a healthy cash reserve to pay for such projects (the exact number varies, depending on a community\xe2\x80\x99s size and the scale of its amenities), but according to Mr. Plumley, some communities have no or limited money in reserve. Your broker will be able to give you that information.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cBe careful what you sign up for, because you could unexpectedly be out a few thousand dollars at any given time,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'ARE YOU WILLING TO PLAY BY THE RULES?'
b'All golf communities have regulations that residents are expected to follow. Mr. Melton said that buyers should be sure to understand what these rules are and decide whether they\xe2\x80\x99re comfortable abiding by them.'
b'One of the more significant rules is whether all residents are required to be members of the golf club. Whether you\xe2\x80\x99re a golfer or not, it may be a smarter move to live in a community where you\xe2\x80\x99re not required to be a member; otherwise, when you look to resell, a potential buyer base will be more limited.'
b'And if you are interested in becoming a member, know what you are signing up for. If you ever move and need to give up your membership, for example, you may be required to pay dues until someone can take it over, which could take a few years.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI know of instances where members have had to pay dues for five years after they\xe2\x80\x99ve moved away,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Melton said.'
b'Also, most communities have design guidelines, and you want to make sure that the aesthetic matches yours. For example, you most likely won\xe2\x80\x99t be allowed to build an art deco home in a community where all the properties are built in a contemporary style.'
b''
b'ASK IF THE GOLF COURSE IS PROTECTED'
b'Is there a chance of your community\xe2\x80\x99s golf course closing so that homes or other structures can be built?'
b'Ask your real-estate agent to find out. In some cases, a golf course is protected by its owner through a conservation easement or deed restriction stating that the land can never be anything but a course. But some courses are not protected, which means that the owners have the right to close them.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t buy in communities where the golf course isn\xe2\x80\x99t protected because your property has the potential to lose 25 percent or more of its value,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Plumley said.'
b''
b'PLAN TO HANG OUT FOR A WHILE'
b'It\xe2\x80\x99s vital to spend a few days actually living at a community you are interested in, Mr. Plumley said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cYou want to make sure that you\xe2\x80\x99re comfortable and like being surrounded by the people who will be your neighbors,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'
b'Most communities offer discounted stays for serious buyers, who should take up the offer and play the golf course, use the pool and dine in the restaurants.'
b'While you\xe2\x80\x99re there, be sure to interact with the staff as much as possible, Mr. Melton said.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIn good golf communities, many of the employees have been around for decades, and you should definitely like them, because they\xe2\x80\x99re the ones who are going to be helping you,\xe2\x80\x9d he said.'

b'By Jeff Shain'
b'It began, in a very real sense, as an oasis in the desert.'
b'When the first shots were struck at what was then the Karl Litten Desert Classic, Emirates Golf Club was flanked by little but sand. Aerial photos from the time showed a stark contrast between the club\xe2\x80\x99s green fairways and various shades of brown outside its borders.'
b'That was 30 years ago. Dubai, United Arab Emirates, was just starting to introduce itself as a tourist destination, and golf offered a natural fit with its winter sunshine and miles of undeveloped acreage. The European Tour was looking to expand and willing to take a chance.'
b'The gamble worked. Enticed by Dubai\xe2\x80\x99s world-class accommodations \xe2\x80\x94 and the occasional appearance fee \xe2\x80\x94 players quickly took notice. In time, the renamed Omega Dubai Desert Classic could boast about having more star power than whatever PGA Tour event it went up against.'
b'Dubai\xe2\x80\x99s success bred a second venture in the Middle East in 1998, the Qatar Masters. Abu Dhabi, another emirate, joined the schedule eight years later, and Dubai added a second event, the DP World Tour Championship, when the tour sought a big-finish season finale.'
b'As the tour returns from its winter break, this week\xe2\x80\x99s Abu Dhabi HSBC Championship presented by EGA is the first of six events set for the Middle East in 2019. That\xe2\x80\x99s 12 percent of the European Tour\xe2\x80\x99s schedule and some of its most attractive stops.'
b'Abu Dhabi this year joins the Rolex Series, a collection of eight showcase events offering purses of at least $7 million. Brooks Koepka, the winner of last year\xe2\x80\x99s United States Open and P.G.A. Championship, and Dustin Johnson will be among the challengers as Tommy Fleetwood seeks a third straight crown. In all, 15 of the top 50 in the world rankings are expected to play.'
b'The tour shifts to Dubai a week later, where two of the past three Masters winners foreshadowed those victories by conquering Emirates Golf Club three months before. In all, on six occasions Dubai champions have won a major later that same year.'
b'Qatar used to make up the third leg of what is called the desert swing, but with the addition of the NBO Oman Open last year and a tournament in Saudi Arabia this month, the tour has opted to break them into two clusters. The Saudi International powered by SBIA finishes the January swing; Oman and Qatar go back-to-back in March.'
b'The DP World Tour Championship also is part of the Rolex Series, bringing the season to a close in November. In all, the six tournaments will hand out about $25 million in prize money.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAcross the board, our golfers love playing in the Middle East,\xe2\x80\x9d Keith Pelley, the European Tour\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive, said when the Saudi International was announced last year. \xe2\x80\x9cThey feel incredibly safe there, they are treated exceptionally well, and all of our host courses are terrific.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The circuit\xe2\x80\x99s Middle East success also empowered tour officials to continue pursuing territorial expansion, with tournaments now spread as far as South Africa, China, Malaysia and India.'
b'Over time, the Middle East has hosted 64 European Tour events. Last year\xe2\x80\x99s five stops in the region drew 22 players who began the year among the top 40 of the world rankings. Johnson ventured to Abu Dhabi for the second consecutive year; Matt Kuchar made his first visit to Abu Dhabi, and Pat Perez to Dubai.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a place I\xe2\x80\x99ve always seen on TV, always kind of admired and wanted to see for myself,\xe2\x80\x9d Kuchar said upon arrival in Abu Dhabi.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s always neat to pick up different things that you just don\xe2\x80\x99t get from TV,\xe2\x80\x9d he added, \xe2\x80\x9cto actually put your hands on things and to see a different culture and see a different place.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was uncharted territory for everyone, from a golf standpoint, when Dubai made the pitch to bring a European Tour event there in 1989.'
b'Emirates Golf Club had just opened; the Majlis course, in fact, was the first grassed golf course in the region. What little golf was played in the Middle East had been done on sand greens.'
b'Sheikh Mohammed bin Rashid al-Maktoum, the ruler of Dubai who would later become prime minister of the United Arab Emirates, envisioned golf as a tourism driver. And the best way to sell the concept was to bring some of the world\xe2\x80\x99s best golfers to play a tournament.'
b'He found a willing ear in Ken Schofield, then the European Tour\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive. For several years, Schofield had been looking for ways to expand the tour at a time when winter left much of Europe unable to partake in the sport.'
b'The tour typically opened its season in April, after the Masters, either in Spain or Italy. There already had been one trial outside the Continent when the Tunisian Open started in 1982. That lasted four years; a Morocco tournament in 1987 didn\xe2\x80\x99t last.'
b'In that sense, the tour wasn\xe2\x80\x99t averse to taking risks. But Dubai was so new to the sport that no one really had an idea what to expect.'
b'Complicating matters was that Emirates Golf Club was then about 15 miles from Dubai\xe2\x80\x99s outer limits. Players had first-class accommodations at the Intercontinental hotel, but almost nothing stood between the course and the city.'
b'The course site was selected for its elevation and its natural terrain \xe2\x80\x94 one could see the Persian Gulf from the eighth green \xe2\x80\x94 but infrastructure was limited. The first edition had just one hospitality tent, two small grandstands and one scoreboard.'
b'Nonetheless, an estimated 7,000 people, many of them European expatriates, came out to watch.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was like having a home game in the Middle East, only with perfect weather and the most magnificent course,\xe2\x80\x9d Phil Parkin, a golfer who is now an analyst, told The National, a newspaper based in Abu Dhabi, in 2015.'
b'Mark James captured the inaugural, beating Peter O\xe2\x80\x99Malley in a playoff.'
b'The 1991 edition was not held because of the Persian Gulf war, but any concerns about the Desert Classic\xe2\x80\x99s future disappeared the next year when Seve Ballesteros made it one of the final victories of his Hall of Fame career.'
b'In 1994, Ernie Els scored his first European Tour win when he cruised to a six-shot romp in Dubai. Five months later, he stamped his name on a bigger stage by winning the U.S. Open at Oakmont.'
b'Tiger Woods has teed it up seven times in Dubai, winning twice. He also helped create some of the event\xe2\x80\x99s more famous images in 2004 when he struck shots from the Burj al Arab hotel\xe2\x80\x99s helipad.'
b'These days, the Dubai skyline is easily seen from the Emirates Golf Club fairways.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s grown from a little unknown dune that nobody knew about back then to one of the tourist destinations of the world,\xe2\x80\x9d said Thomas Bjorn, last year\xe2\x80\x99s winning European Ryder Cup captain, who made his Dubai debut in 1996.'
b'Seeing Dubai\xe2\x80\x99s success, the Qatar Masters made its debut in 1998 with Andrew Coltart taking home the trophy. Adam Scott has won it twice, as have Paul Lawrie and Branden Grace.'
b'The Abu Dhabi Golf Championship came along in 2006, with five of the first six titles split between Martin Kaymer (three) and Paul Casey (two). The DP World Tour Championship began in 2009, with Rory McIlroy and Henrik Stenson each winning twice.'
b'Even with the additions of Oman and Saudi Arabia, Pelley, the European Tour\xe2\x80\x99s chief executive, hinted that the Middle East expansion may not be done. Bahrain was on the schedule for one year, hosting the short-lived Volvo Golf Champions in 2011 before the Arab Spring uprisings prompted organizers to move the 2012 event.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo be honest, in the Middle East we\xe2\x80\x99re open to hosting tournaments in any countries that want to support golf,\xe2\x80\x9d Pelley said. \xe2\x80\x9cAt the moment we have six events, but could we feasibly have another one in there? I think so.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'Supported by'
b'By Richard Goldstein'
b'Gene Littler, a quietly outstanding golfer who was known as Gene the Machine for an uncommonly smooth and consistent swing that propelled him to the 1961 United States Open championship, died on Friday in San Diego. He was 88.'
b'His death was announced by the PGA Tour. His son, Curt, told The San Diego Union-Tribune that he had neuropathy in his legs and had had several falls. In 1972, Littler had surgery for lymph cancer that had seemingly ended his career.'
b'In his prime, though self-taught, he had \xe2\x80\x9ca perfect swing,\xe2\x80\x9d said Gene Sarazen, a winner of seven major championships. \xe2\x80\x9cLike Sam Snead\xe2\x80\x99s, only better.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Littler was typically self-effacing in assessing his form. \xe2\x80\x9cI just put the ball down and hit,\xe2\x80\x9d he once said.'
b'Unassuming and devoid of glamour in an era dominated by Arnold Palmer, Jack Nicklaus and Gary Player, and relatively unimposing at 5 foot 9 and 160 pounds or so, Littler simply went about winning tournaments: 29 on the PGA Tour and another eight on what was then the Senior PGA Tour.'
b'Littler, who lost two other majors in playoffs and another by one stroke, was a seven-time Ryder Cup player and was inducted into the World Golf Hall of Fame in 1990.'
b'Littler was virtually ignored by the galleries in the early stages of the 1961 United State Open\xe2\x80\x99s final round at Oakland Hills in Michigan. He was among a pack chasing Doug Sanders, who was three shots ahead after the third round, and he had injured a rib earlier in the year, sidelining him for two months. He had won a total of $116 in his first five tournaments of 1961. Not only that, but Littler needed to adjust his widely envied swing a few days before the tournament.'
b'As Littler later told it, Ted Kroll, a fellow professional, \xe2\x80\x9ctold me to hit the ball more directly, or more upright.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Littler added, \xe2\x80\x9cI had a tendency to swing flat.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It was Littler\xe2\x80\x99s brilliant putting that carried him to victory at Oakland Hills, whose undulating greens frustrated many of the other contenders. He one-putted on six holes of the final round and needed only the customary two putts at the others, and he sank 15-foot putts at Nos. 7 and 13. After hitting into a bunker guarding the green on the 18th hole, he two-putted for a bogey 5 and a two-under-par 68 that bested Sanders and Bob Goalby by a shot.'
b'Gene Alec Littler was born on July 21, 1930, in San Diego and grew to love golf while playing on area courses. He graduated from San Diego State University and then entered the Navy. He won the United States Amateur and played in the Walker Cup amateur competition between the United States and a British-Irish team in 1953.'
b'The prominent golf writer Herbert Warren Wind was impressed by the fluidity of such a young player\xe2\x80\x99s swing.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cGene took the club back with a very, very slow, easy, relaxed rhythm, then paused a lazy second at the top before droning slowly down into the ball, delaying his accelerated hitting action until the very last moment when the club head was only two feet or so from the ball,\xe2\x80\x9d Wind wrote in 1955 in Sports Illustrated.'
b'While still an amateur, Littler won the San Diego Open in January 1954, and he turned pro soon afterward. He almost won the United States Open in June 1954, losing to Ed Furgol by one stroke, and then won four tournaments in 1955. He captured the Tournament of Champions in Las Vegas three consecutive times, from 1955 to 1957. Littler lost to Billy Casper, a friend since their boyhood in San Diego, in an 18-hole playoff at the 1970 Masters.'
b'Two years later, Littler was found to have lymph cancer, requiring surgery. Much of the muscular structure on his left side was removed. But through arduous rehabilitation, he was able to regain the use of his left arm and rejoin the tour. He won the St. Louis Children\xe2\x80\x99s Hospital Classic in July 1973 and received the Ben Hogan Award as comeback player of the year and the Bob Jones Award for distinguished sportsmanship in golf.'
b'Littler went to a playoff at the 1977 P.G.A. Championship at Pebble Beach, losing to Lanny Wadkins on the third hole of sudden death after leading by five strokes with nine holes to play.'
b'He retired from the PGA Tour after that season and joined the fledgling Senior PGA Tour in 1981. Three years later he fell from a ladder while working on one of his antique cars and fractured his left arm, which was already weakened from cancer surgery. But he won six times on the Senior Tour after that.'
b'In addition to his son, survivors include his wife, Shirley, and a daughter, Suzanne.'
b'For all his achievements, and all the admiration for his swing, Littler struggled with self-doubt.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI never gave myself enough credit,\xe2\x80\x9d he told The Union-Tribune in 1987. \xe2\x80\x9cIf I could change anything, I\xe2\x80\x99d change my attitude. I\xe2\x80\x99d come out again like Nicklaus or Palmer. I think I had a lot of ability but I never had what those guys had, that confidence.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The World Golf Hall of Fame quoted him once saying: \xe2\x80\x9cI drew a big gallery today. I was paired with Palmer.\xe2\x80\x9d'

Last year's final round of the British Open on NBC averaged 6.48 million, when Woods was in contention, and the final day of the Ryder Cup from Paris averaged 2.67 million."

b'By Karen Crouse'
b'PEBBLE BEACH, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 The AT&T Pebble Beach Pro-Am never fails to rattle Darius Rucker\xe2\x80\x99s nerves. This year though, Rucker, the three-time Grammy Award winning musician, had more to fret about than hitting a spectator or getting in the way of his pro partner, Kenny Perry.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow you\xe2\x80\x99re scared that somebody\xe2\x80\x99s going to come call a rules violation on you with something that you don\xe2\x80\x99t know about,\xe2\x80\x9d Rucker said before the tournament began last week.'
b'The pros are just as worried. The United States Golf Association and the R&A revised the sport\xe2\x80\x99s rule book to simplify the game and speed up the pace of play. But so far the changes, which took effect at the start of 2019, have been harder to follow than a game of Simon Says.'
b'In the few weeks since the modifications took effect, players have repeatedly sought guidance from the nearest rules official, their caddies or pieces of paper tucked inside their golf bags, undermining for now, at least, the stated intention of making things simpler and faster.'
b'And it\xe2\x80\x99s adding an extra bit of hesitancy to the pros\xe2\x80\x99 trip through the course. During a rain-sodden second round at Pebble Beach on Friday, Hunter Mahan was forced to consult a tournament-issued rules sheet before touching his ball. \xe2\x80\x9cWe thought we knew what the rule was,\xe2\x80\x9d Mahan said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut there\xe2\x80\x99s no clarity, so having an official or actually having it written down is the only true clarification.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'One new rule has lowered the height from which players make a drop: it is now from the knees, rather than the shoulders, a change that the former men\xe2\x80\x99s world No. 1 Adam Scott described as awkward. Whenever he bends over or squats with the ball, he can\xe2\x80\x99t help but imagine rules officials assigned to monitor potential rules violations squinting at their screens, scrutinizing his release down to the inch.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey\xe2\x80\x99ve just written more gray areas into the game that were not necessary,\xe2\x80\x9d said Scott, who won\xe2\x80\x99t make a drop without asking his caddie or a nearby official if he has the height right.'
b'Even those enforcing the rules have been confused about how to interpret them. During the second round of the Phoenix Open earlier this month, Denny McCarthy was assessed a two-stroke penalty under Rule 10.2b(4), a new regulation that prohibits caddies from standing behind players as they line up for their shots.'
b'While McCarthy took a few practice swings, his caddie stood behind him. McCarthy stepped away before hitting the shot, and when he came back to the ball and set his stance, his caddie was standing off to the side. The next day, the PGA Tour announced that it had rescinded the penalty after reviewing McCarthy\xe2\x80\x99s actions, and his score of 67 became a 65.'
b'Somewhat lost in the turbulence created by the alignment rule in the men\xe2\x80\x99s game is the fact that the change was seen as directed at the L.P.G.A., where caddies lining up players had been more common. Brittany Lincicome, an eight-time L.P.G.A. tour winner and two-time major champion, said she was glad \xe2\x80\x9cit wasn\xe2\x80\x99t one of us\xe2\x80\x9d who became the rule\xe2\x80\x99s first victim.'
b'After the caddie-alignment episode with McCarthy, and several similar situations involving other players, the U.S.G.A. and the R&A issued a clarification: If players reset their stances after their caddies have surveyed a shot, there is no penalty.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cGoing in, we knew there were certain things that were going to come up that you\xe2\x80\x99d say, \xe2\x80\x98We\xe2\x80\x99re not sure we contemplated this or the intention was never to have this outcome,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d Mike Davis, the chief executive of the U.S.G.A. told The Global Golf Post. He added, \xe2\x80\x9cAll in all, in terms of how they\xe2\x80\x99re being perceive around the globe, it\xe2\x80\x99s very positive.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'That wasn\xe2\x80\x99t the case for Rickie Fowler, who took dead aim at the caddie-alignment rule during the Phoenix Open. \xe2\x80\x9cYou\xe2\x80\x99re talking about growing the game and making things play faster and whatnot,\xe2\x80\x9d he said, \xe2\x80\x9cbut that\xe2\x80\x99s not growing the game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Adding to Fowler\xe2\x80\x99s exasperation was a run-in with one of the rule book\xe2\x80\x99s unchanged regulations on the Sunday of the tournament. He took a one-stroke penalty for hitting a shot into the water, then absorbed another one-stroke penalty after his ball rolled back into the hazard several seconds after he walked toward the green to survey his chip.'
b'After carding a triple bogey, Fowler, in a show of gallows humor, petitioned the rules official, Slugger White, for a rules modification.'
b'Fowler hung on to win, but Tony Finau, who watched the round unfold on television after missing the cut, saw the gravity in Fowler\xe2\x80\x99s joking.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAs I watched that transpire, I couldn\xe2\x80\x99t help but think, This is not what the integrity of the game is about,\xe2\x80\x9d Finau said. \xe2\x80\x9cHe didn\xe2\x80\x99t do anything for that ball to move.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'One player\xe2\x80\x99s mishap is another\xe2\x80\x99s teachable moment. An L.P.G.A. rules official disseminated the video of Fowler playing the hole, noting that he could have avoided the second penalty by making his first two drops, then using a tee to mark the spot where he intended to place the ball. After surveying his shot, he could have then replaced the tee with his ball before taking his shot.'
b'Breaking up the sequence of drop-drop-place like that was illuminating to Lincicome: \xe2\x80\x9cI didn\xe2\x80\x99t even know that was a thing,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Another new wrinkle on the course this year is using the flagstick as a backboard on putts; to speed up play, golfers can leave the pin in no matter where they are on the course, including the green. Anticipating the outcome, Bryson DeChambeau said last year, \xe2\x80\x9cThe U.S.G.A.\xe2\x80\x99s going to have to go back on that one, like, \xe2\x80\x98No! We made the hole bigger!\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'It sure has seemed that way to Scott, who ranked 165th on tour in 2018 in strokes-gained putting. Putting with the flagstick in the hole, he is ranked No. 26. \xe2\x80\x9cTo be honest,\xe2\x80\x9d Scott said, \xe2\x80\x9cit almost changes the whole aim of the game. It\xe2\x80\x99s to hit the pin, not hole the putt.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'He added, \xe2\x80\x9cIt takes speed out of your head so much. It even takes some reading of the green out.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'DeChambeau has a point. The game\xe2\x80\x99s governing bodies might be eager to simplify the rules, but their intent was never to make the game easier.'
b'And in the end, have they really simplified anything?'
b'When Scott looks at the remaining layers of rules as well as the lingering and newfound confusion, he, like Fowler, wonders how it is growing the game. Imagine picking up an unfamiliar board game, he said, and opening the box to find 84 pages of rules. Would you bother playing it?'
b'Now picture the same game, with only five or six rules to learn to start out. Which version would you find more appealing?'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s have all the rules on the back of the scorecard for people to get into the game of golf,\xe2\x80\x9d Scott said, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cAnd then as you get playing more you can maybe learn some finer points of this very complex game.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Though Jay Monahan, the P.G.A. commissioner, said last week that he felt proud of how quickly and nimbly the alignment rule confusion was addressed, Scott disagreed.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe haven\xe2\x80\x99t had a lot of changes in golf in the history of the game , and we\xe2\x80\x99ve had a lot recently \xe2\x80\x94 rules changing weekly in some cases \xe2\x80\x94 and it\xe2\x80\x99s crazy,\xe2\x80\x9d Scott said.'
b'He added, \xe2\x80\x9cI think we\xe2\x80\x99re becoming the laughingstock.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'By Reuters'
b"AUGUSTA, GA \xe2\x80\x94 Tommy Fleetwood may already be one of golf's most recognizable players but the mop-topped Englishman is determined to be marked out as winner rather than for a great head of hair."
b'Looking more like a member of Hall of Fame rock band Fleetwood Mac than the PGA Tour, the 28-year-old, with his scruffy beard and long locks spilling out from under a baseball cap, was easily distinguishable from the cookie cutter golfing crowd getting in some practice on Monday at Augusta National ahead of the Masters.'
b'Considering Fleetwood\'s PGA Tour resume does not yet include a title, he would not have drawn much attention had it not been for his "better to burn out than fade away" approach to tournament play which has amplified his rocker image.'
b'That "all in" attitude was on full display during the final round of the Players Championship last month when he was trailing Rory McIlroy by two strokes with two holes to play. Fleetwood attacked the pin on the infamous 17th island green and paid the price as his title hopes ended in a watery grave.'
b'"I don\'t know why people would expect me to play for the middle of the green if I had a chance of catching Rory," Fleetwood told reporters. "Maybe that\'s my difference than some other people, I\'m always going to play to win.'
b'"Not that golf will ever define me as a person but I\'m never going to look back on my career and say, oh, I finished third at the Players, that was a good week. Or, oh, I finished top five at the Masters, I made a couple of nice pars on the last to finish top five. '
b'"That\'s probably something I\'ll never say to my kids or grandkids. That\'s not something to be that proud of.'
b'"Winning is what it\'s all about."'
b"While Fleetwood is still chasing a maiden PGA Tour title, he does know his way to the winner's circle with four victories on the European Tour."
b"He has regularly featured on the leaderboard at majors, including a runner-up finish at last year's U.S. Open and has shown good form this season with three top 10s."
b'More importantly Fleetwood believes his Masters apprenticeship has reached the point where he can fight for a green jacket.'
b'After missing the cut in his first visit to Augusta in 2017, Fleetwood improved to a 17th place finish last year. He showed signs that he was getting comfortable with the layout after carding a six-under 66 in the third round.'
b'"Year one, it\'s all so new," said Fleetwood. "Year two, you\'ve been here already, so you\'re more comfortable with it and it just kind of progresses. '
b'"There\'s a different atmosphere.'
b'"It\'s the first major of the year and ... everything that\'s happened before just doesn\'t really matter.'
b'"You know, this is it."'

b"AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 Augusta National chairman Fred Ridley on Wednesday threw cold water on the idea of one day hosting a women's Masters alongside the men's major."
b"Augusta National, which did not have a woman member until seven years ago, held its first women's tournament last week on the same course that will play host to the men's major."
b"Ridley, however, said the club has no plans to take another step and develop a women's Masters."
b'"To date, all of our grow-the-game initiatives have been focused on amateur golf and amateur golfers," said Ridley during the Augusta National chairman\'s annual address on Wednesday. '
b'"In this particular case, we elected to conduct a women\'s amateur tournament for really that same reason, but we really wanted this to continue in a grow-the-game sort of mode.'
b'"As to what we might do next, I\'m still thinking about last Saturday, so I\'ll start thinking about that next week."'
b"For many the next logical step is for Augusta to organize a women's Masters. The idea, however, does not seem to excite the Augusta membership."
b"While Augusta National is best known as the home of the Masters, Ridley believes the club is better serving the amateur roots of co-founders Clifford Roberts and Bobby Jones and developing the sport by giving its name to a women's amateur competition."
b'"I think part of that kind of goes back to history and that is that Augusta National was founded, co-founded by the greatest amateur of all time," said Ridley. '
b"After opening its doors to women members in 2012, Augusta National has since made efforts to promote and develop women's golf, but some in the game remain frustrated by what they see as the painfully slow pace of change."
b"Asked if the club's failure to confront its restrictive policies had stunted the growth of the women's game, Ridley said they could have done better. "
b'"No matter what the issue is, you know, we can always look back and say we could do better," said Ridley. "No question. '
b'"But what my focus is, is on the future and where we are now and where we want to go. We learn from the past. '
b'"But what I think is most productive is to look at where we are today, realize that throughout the history of this club, we have promoted the game and we have now identified a really important segment, the fastest growing segment of the game - that we can help make a difference."'

b'(Reuters) - Dutchman Daan Huizing made nine birdies to take the lead in the first round of the Jordan Mixed Open, the first professional tournament with men and women competing against each other for the same prize, on Thursday. '
b"Huizing shot an eight-under 64 in Aqaba to lead England's Meghan MacLaren, a Ladies European Tour winner, and her compatriot Jack Senior by one stroke."
b'Forty professionals and one amateur player each from the Challenge Tour, the over-50s Tour and the Ladies European Tour are in the field, competing for a prize fund of around $400,000.'
b'"Today was pretty complete and I was shaping the ball nicely, both ways, which is something I\'ve worked on very hard over the winter," Huizing told reporters.'
b'"I made some good putts and mentally I was in good shape as well, sticking to my process, so there are a lot of good signs and I\'m looking forward to tomorrow."'
b"MacLaren, who sparked debate in January over the disparity in pay between men's and women's events, was happy to finish among the leaders after setting the early clubhouse target."
b'"If I\'m going to write about it and talk about it all the time, then I better back it up with my golf," MacLaren, the only woman to finish in the top 10, said. "If I\'m up there it means the girls can take advantage.'
b'"I\'m delighted to do it at this tournament because hopefully it will send a message. But any time you shoot seven under in any tournament you\'re not going to be too far off the lead."'
b'The course was designed by Australian Greg Norman who was world number one for over 300 weeks in the 1980s and 1990s.'
b'"To construct a format in which women and men compete together over the same course is an impressive feat," Norman said in a statement.'
b'"There is no doubt that events that showcase golfing talent regardless of gender, such as the Jordan Mixed Open... are the future of the game."'
b'The Challenge Tour players are playing from tees making up a 7,152-yard course, the seniors cover 6,601 yards and the women 6,139 yards.'
b'"Our first and primary priority was to engineer a format that could showcase golfing talent regardless of gender," director of operations Chris White said.'
b'"This not only means taking into consideration carry yardages, both off the tee and throughout the player\'s whole bag, but also the positioning of bunkers and hazards."'
b"Although the Jordan tournament is the first, official mixed gender tournament, men and women have competed against each other previously, most notably at the Wendy's 3-Tour Challenge, a single-day event which ran from 1992-2013."
b' (Reporting by Rohith Nair in Bengaluru, editing by Ed Osmond and Christian Radnedge)'
