b'By Karen Crouse'
b'NAUCALPAN DE JU\xc3\x81REZ, Mexico \xe2\x80\x94 Nine holes into his record-tying round Sunday, Justin Thomas bumped into Rory McIlroy, who was waiting to tee off on the first hole at Club de Golf Chapultepec. He said he asked McIlroy how he thought the afternoon would go.'
b'McIlroy began the final day of the Mexico Championship four strokes behind Dustin Johnson, a deficit that was daunting but hardly insurmountable; the previous Sunday, J. B. Holmes charged from four strokes back to beat Thomas at the Genesis Open.'
b'McIlroy told Thomas it would be hard to catch Johnson because of how well he was playing, a prediction that proved to be hit-the-flagstick accurate. Johnson, who was sixth on the PGA Tour in driving distance last year, ranked first in this week\xe2\x80\x99s field in putting. It was an unbeatable combination as Johnson closed with a five-under-par 66 to finish five strokes clear of McIlroy, who posted a 67.'
b'Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s 72-hole total in this World Golf Championships event outside Mexico City was 19 under. McIlroy finished at 16 under, which would have been good enough to win each of the previous two years that the tournament was held here. On Sunday, all it got McIlroy was a five-stroke cushion over the third-place finishers: Paul Casey (65), Ian Poulter (68) and Kiradech Aphibarnrat (68).'
b'Tiger Woods recorded a 69 to finish in a four-way tie for 10th at eight under.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was sort of like there was two different golf tournaments going on and I won the second one,\xe2\x80\x9d said McIlroy, who has posted top-five finishes in all four of his tour starts in 2019.'
b'Thomas, who played in the first group off the back nine, took advantage of pristine greens and nonexistent pressure to record a 62, tying his year-old course record, vaulting him into ninth. His score represented a 13-stroke improvement over his final 18 last Sunday at Riviera Country Club.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI would sure play a lot of money to switch the two,\xe2\x80\x9d Thomas said with a smile. \xe2\x80\x9cI would gladly take a 50th place this week to win last week.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Johnson, 34, became the first player since Davis Love III in 2008 to reach 20 PGA Tour titles. \xe2\x80\x9cTo get 20 wins out here is very difficult, and do it before I turn 35 is pretty incredible,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said, adding, \xe2\x80\x9cThis is a big one for me, and it gives me a lot of confidence for the rest of the year.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Johnson is not lacking for confidence. He has two victories and a tie for ninth in his last four starts. He also extended his streak of seasons with at least one tour title to 12, an emphatic argument for his inclusion among the finest players in the men\xe2\x80\x99s game (Jack Nicklaus and Arnold Palmer share the record at 17, one better than Billy Casper and three more than Woods).'
b'McIlroy, 29, also extended a streak, this one more enigmatic. Since January of last year, he has played his way into the last group for the final round eight times \xe2\x80\x94 without emerging triumphant. McIlroy\xe2\x80\x99s lone title run in that stretch came at Bay Hill last March when he started the final round in the next-to-last group.'
b'To mount a charge, McIlroy needed to get off to the kind of hot start engineered by Casey, who teed off four groups ahead and birdied the first three holes. Johnson started shakily, playing the first five holes in one over, but McIlroy, despite making a birdie at the second, could not swing the momentum his way. He did not find a fairway off the tee until the eighth hole and he missed a birdie putt of 11 feet on the first hole and a 6-footer for par on the fourth.'
b'After playing the first nine in one over, McIlroy settled for par on No. 10, which Johnson birdied. At that point, McIlroy said, his caddie, Harry Diamond, told him to forget about trying to catch Johnson and concentrate on consolidating second place.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI knew at that point that I didn\xe2\x80\x99t have a chance; D. J. was playing too well,\xe2\x80\x9d McIlroy said.'
b'McIlroy covered the final eight holes in five under and all he could do was equal Johnson\xe2\x80\x99s final-nine 31.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI felt like I was standing still,\xe2\x80\x9d McIlroy said with a laugh. \xe2\x80\x9cI was making birdies and going nowhere.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The other member of the final threesome on Sunday was Patrick Reed, who was grouped with McIlroy on Sunday at last year\xe2\x80\x99s Masters and claimed the green jacket with a 71 to McIlroy\xe2\x80\x99s 74. That was McIlroy\xe2\x80\x99s second cubic zirconia in the lustrous string. The fourth was the World Golf Championships event in Ohio, where he could not overcome Thomas\xe2\x80\x99s three-stroke advantage. The sixth was the Tour Championship, where he started three behind Woods. The seventh was the Tournament of Champions, where Xander Schauffele shot a 62 to leapfrog into first.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve played well, I\xe2\x80\x99ve done what I\xe2\x80\x99ve wanted to do and needed to do,\xe2\x80\x9d McIlroy said, adding: \xe2\x80\x9cMy game\xe2\x80\x99s right there. I\xe2\x80\x99m really happy with everything. I\xe2\x80\x99ve just got to stay patient, look at the positives and just keep persisting and putting myself in positions, and sooner or later hopefully it will go my way.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Golf could not be going much better for Johnson, who became the fifth player in the last 50 years to collect 20 wins before his 35th birthday, joining Woods, Phil Mickelson, Tom Watson and Johnny Miller.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s very sweet,\xe2\x80\x9d Johnson said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a lot of hard to get here, but it feels really good. I\xe2\x80\x99m very proud of myself.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'An earlier version of this article referred incorrectly to a milestone reached by Dustin Johnson. He is the fifth golfer int he 50 years to collect 20 wins before his 35th birthday, not the fifth golfer over all to do so.'

b'NAUCALPAN DE JU\xc3\x81REZ, Mexico \xe2\x80\x94 From where he stood on the fairway on the par-5 15th hole, all Tiger Woods could see on Saturday were the possibilities. He was eight under par for the tournament and stalking a final-round, final-threesome grouping in his Mexico Championship debut.'
b'Standing several yards from Woods, also in the fairway, John Sutcliffe, who is covering the tournament for ESPN and ESPN Deportes, could see all the way to Sunday night.'
b'Sutcliffe, who grew up in a house along the 10th hole of the course, Club de Golf Chapultepec, said, \xe2\x80\x9cI was thinking, when it gets to be the final hole of the tournament, maybe the Tiger roar will be in Spanish.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But elsewhere on the course, Dustin Johnson was pulling away from the field, and No. 15 was about to undo Woods.'
b'His 54-hole total of six under left him tied for ninth in this World Golf Championships event, well out of the final group and 10 strokes behind Johnson, who carded a 66 for a four-shot lead over his closest competitor, Rory McIlroy.'
b'Still the headliner is indisputably Woods, who took 24 years and 381 starts to make his first appearance as a professional in Mexico.'
b'He has drawn large, ardent crowds here, just outside Mexico City. After waiting so long to see Woods up close, the followers were not about to let a few errant swings or wayward putts ruin the festive mood. On Saturday, they shouted things like, \xe2\x80\x9cTiger, Marry My Sister!\xe2\x80\x9d and serenaded him with cries of \xe2\x80\x9cTiger\xe2\x80\x9d until he disappeared into the scoring room.'
b'Woods\xe2\x80\x99s caddie, Joe LaCava, described Woods as \xe2\x80\x9clike Michael Jordan down here\xe2\x80\x9d and said the fans were so excited to see him in person, \xe2\x80\x9cthey didn\xe2\x80\x99t even care where the shots were going.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'At 15, his second shot found a greenside bunker, and he chunked his next shot out of the sand, leaving him a 25-footer for birdie. Woods\xe2\x80\x99s first putt rolled four feet past the hole, and he three-putted from there for a double-bogey 7. It was the 12th four-putt of his career, and it killed momentum. He made bogey on the next hole \xe2\x80\x94 also after his tee shot found the fairway \xe2\x80\x94 before salvaging a 1-under 70 with a closing birdie.'
b'One of the fans who followed Woods for each of his first three rounds was Sebastian Mondragon, 13, who said he started playing golf when he was 9. He ran from spot to spot, positioning himself so he could try to draw Woods\xe2\x80\x99s attention to a handmade sign that featured the face of a tiger and the exhortation, \xe2\x80\x9cLet\xe2\x80\x99s Go, Tiger.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'As Woods walked from the eighth green to the ninth tee, Mondragon stood at the front of the rope line. He waved the sign and shouted Woods\xe2\x80\x99s name, but the 14-time major champion walked past, staring straight ahead.'
b'Mondragon said he hoped that watching Woods would offer some pointers. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat I\xe2\x80\x99ve learned,\xe2\x80\x9d Mondragon said, \xe2\x80\x9cis he has a very good focus.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Woods had a lot to process as he headed to the ninth tee. He bent his 9-iron on the eighth hole when he hit a tree during his swing, so the club was out of commission for the rest of the round. He sorely missed it on the 14th hole, when he had the perfect distance for a 9-iron approach.'
b'Using his pitching wedge instead, Woods came up short but still managed par. On the 16th hole, LaCava said, Woods had to lay back off the tee to set up an 8-iron approach.'
b'After the round, Woods, 43, received therapy on his surgically repaired back, LaCava said that after that, his boss intended to meet with a club repairer in hopes of fixing his 9-iron in time for Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s round.'
b'Whatever happens in the final 18 holes, Woods\xe2\x80\x99s debut here will go down as an unqualified hit. In his gallery Saturday was a couple, originally from Portugal, who are living in Mexico City. This was their first time at a golf tournament, they said, and they stopped along the ninth fairway so the husband, Pedro Caixinha, could take a photograph of his wife, Anabela David, with Woods walking in the background.'
b'Caixinha described the photograph as \xe2\x80\x9ca souvenir.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Before the tournament, Sutcliffe told Woods that his presence would make this the most important week in the golf course\xe2\x80\x99s nearly 100-year history. Then he presented Woods with his own souvenir: a bottle of tequila.'

b'On Golf'
b'By Bill Pennington'
b'AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 If Tiger Woods\xe2\x80\x99s victory at the 2019 Masters is among the greatest comebacks in sports history \xe2\x80\x94 and it is at least a leading candidate \xe2\x80\x94 its origin will forever be traced to what happened on the 12th hole on Sunday when the old Tiger Woods suddenly reappeared at a major championship for the first time in 11 years.'
b'It was far more than a golf hole. It was psychological drama, the instant a former champion reclaimed his domain, and the kind of seminal moment that helps rewrite a sport\xe2\x80\x99s history.'
b'Among the many things that Woods lost in his public fall from grace a decade ago, one of the most obvious was his steely resolve. Gone was the inimitable fortitude that had allowed him to rise above \xe2\x80\x94 and then put away \xe2\x80\x94 opponents in the crucible of high-pressure competitions.'
b'It was whittled over time, but it had unquestionably been missing. In the 14 minutes that began at 12:30 p.m. Sunday at Augusta National Golf Club, the famous Woods intimidation factor was rejuvenated. About 90 minutes later, when Woods was trying on a fifth green Masters jacket and celebrating a 15th major golf championship, it had been fully restored.'
b'And everyone in the field knew it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTiger\xe2\x80\x99s back,\xe2\x80\x9d said Brooks Koepka, the two-time defending United States Open champion.'
b'The opening episode of the day\xe2\x80\x99s turning-point chapter was when Koepka and Ian Poulter, who were playing in the group ahead of Woods, each fell victim to the mental and physical pressure exacted by the mystifying 12th hole. Each dunked his tee shot in Rae\xe2\x80\x99s Creek, which separates the green from the tee 158 yards away.'
b'Koepka and Poulter, who had been challenging for the lead, each double bogeyed and never recovered completely. Then Francesco Molinari, who had a two-stroke lead over Woods and was playing in his group, misjudged and mis-hit his tee shot at the 12th hole into the water. So did Tony Finau, also playing with Woods, and only one stroke behind him at the time.'
b'Woods, playing the hole for the 86th time at the Masters, knew to aim more to the left and used enough club to fight through the tricky breeze to position his ball safely in the center of the green.'
b'But what happened next is what truly altered the mood and kick-started Woods\xe2\x80\x99s charge to victory.'
b'Woods walked over the Hogan bridge and stood defiantly on the 12th green glaring back at Finau and Molinari as they dejectedly stood on the other side of the water, rummaging through their bags for another ball and club to once again try to traverse the creek.'
b'Woods was in their line of sight, standing with his arms crossed or one hand on his hip. He continued to stare in their direction with an expression that seemed to say: \xe2\x80\x9cCan you hurry up? I\xe2\x80\x99ve got a tournament to win.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Molinari and Finau eventually put their third shots on the green. Woods subsequently putted out for his par. Looking thunderstruck, Molinari and Finau missed bogey putts that led to matching double bogeys.'
b'With the tournament on the line, four players at the top of the leaderboard had each dropped two strokes. It was 12:44 p.m. and Woods was tied for the lead in the Masters.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt all flipped on 12; the mistake Francesco made there let a lot of guys back into the tournament, myself included,\xe2\x80\x9d Woods said later. He added with a devilish smile: \xe2\x80\x9cIt helps to be experienced. That\xe2\x80\x99s all I was concentrating on. Don\xe2\x80\x99t be fooled. The other guys ended up short.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'And what of the death stare from the 12th green as he waited for his chief rivals to sort out their troubles at the very center of the classically crucial Amen Corner?'
b'Woods let his actions speak for themselves.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a tough hole,\xe2\x80\x9d is all he said.'
b'It is especially tough if Tiger Woods, once again commanding and authoritative, is shooting you daggers.'
b'Woods\xe2\x80\x99s victory rekindles a debate that had been dormant for years: whether Jack Nicklaus\xe2\x80\x99s record of 18 major championships can yet be surpassed.'
b'Woods wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t opine on that topic, either.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s a little soon right now, I\xe2\x80\x99m just enjoying the 15th,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m sure I\xe2\x80\x99ll think about a little down the road.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Woods was hoarse from the primal-like screams he unleashed after tapping in the final putt on the 18th hole to secure his one-stroke victory. At that moment, he had celebrated uproariously around the green, with an unbridled elation and childlike spontaneity that he rarely displayed when he was 20 years younger.'
b'Afterward, an ever-smiling Woods, 43, was even willing to assess his legacy, something he has always been loath to do.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ve driven a lot more youth to the game,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cYou know, a lot of the guys that are on the tour now, they\xe2\x80\x99re training. They are getting bigger, stronger, faster and more athletic.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThey are hitting the ball prodigious distances, and a little bit of that\xe2\x80\x99s probably attributed to what I did.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'But Woods had not bequeathed his dogged determination or his ability to impart his will on the outcome of golf tournaments. It had been missing from the game. At the 12th hole on Sunday, it resurfaced and changed the face of the 2019 Masters.'
b'Now the sports world will wait to see if it eventually rewrites golf history.'
b'An earlier version of this article misstated the time Tiger Woods first led the Masters. He shared the lead at times during the first and third rounds; he was not tied for the lead for the first time in the tournament at 12:44 p.m. Sunday.'

b'By The Associated Press'
b"AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 Valentino Dixon's introduction to golf came when the warden dropped by his 6-by-10 cell at Attica Correctional Facility in New York with a photo of the iconic 12th hole at Augusta National and a simple request."
b'Could Dixon draw the hole with his colored pencils?'
b'The warden knew Dixon had the talent. He certainly had the time.'
b'"I hadn\'t heard of the 12th hole, let alone Augusta National," Dixon said. "Nothing about golf. Never paid a second of time to golf, it was always football or basketball where I come from."'
b"Dixon didn't want to disappoint the warden while serving 39 years-to-life after being convicted of killing a man at a street party in his hometown of Buffalo in 1991. The warden, after all, held great sway over his living conditions in one of the nation's most notorious \xe2\x80\x94 and dangerous \xe2\x80\x94 prisons."
b'But the last thing he wanted to do was irritate his fellow inmates.'
b'"They might take my credibility card away, they may say he\'s drawing golf courses, what\'s going on here," Dixon said. "You don\'t want people to think, hey, he\'s too close with the administration and this prison."'
b'So Dixon set about drawing. Some times that went on for 15 hours, with Dixon finding solace drawing the colors of the grass against the brilliantly white sand and blue sky .'
b"The warden loved the image, though that's hardly where this story ends. Dixon made more golf course drawings, hundreds of them from pictures he saw in Golf Digest and other magazines."
b"It wasn't long before they found other eyes."
b'In their reflection, he found support and more believers in his innocence . His conviction was vacated last September, but not before he had spent 27 years in prison.'
b'This week, Dixon found himself in a place far removed from his former home . He was at Augusta National for the Masters; it was both eerily familiar and strikingly foreign to him.'
b"He walked down to Amen Corner and saw the 12th hole he knew only from pictures. He met Tiger Woods and Jack Nicklaus, whom he'd only seen in magazines."
b'It felt like home. The drawings had taken him here day after endless day, when there seemed no end in sight and no reason for hope.'
b'"I just wanted to cry," Dixon said. "I mean inside I was crying but I held back the tears, you know, because it\'s just so much more remarkable and awesome in person. And I\'ve drawn that 12th hole about eight or nine times and it\'s nothing like seeing it in person \xe2\x80\x94 nothing. It\'s just like the most wonderful thing that I can see in the world right now."'
b'After spending more than half his life in prison, Dixon might still be there if not for his art. He might be protesting his innocence, too, if not for a Golf Digest writer who answered his letter in 2011 as a submission to a monthly narrative called "How Golf Saved My Life."'
b'"Golf is saving my life right now because I had almost 20 years then and I was on borrowed time myself," Dixon said. "I didn\'t know if I was going to live one day to see it to the next."'
b"Some of his friends in Attica didn't. They took their own lives."
b'"I made sure that I kept my sanity," he said. "You know people lose their way."'
b"Golf Digest's Max Adler set the wheels of justice in motion when he replied to Dixon's letter. Seven more years passed before he was finally free."
b'"I was actually an art major in college, so it\'s like this is golf and art and the human condition all coming together," Adler said. "I\'m of course skeptical that this guy is wrongfully convicted, but the fact that art was sort of a redemptive force for him. I thought I\'d like to know more about that."'
b"Adler visited Dixon inside Attica, and saw his colored pencils ground down to the nub. His daughter Valentina's efforts gathered more momentum as, first, two attorneys got involved and then even more when students from Georgetown University's Prison Reform Project took up the cause. The final piece of the puzzle fell into place when a new prosecutor took over in Erie County and reviewed the case."
b'Another man already incarcerated pleaded guilty to the murder.'
b'"Twenty-seven years, it\'s just a miracle," Adler said. "And it\'s a miracle that we ever even heard from him."'
b'Dixon walked out of prison on a day filled with bright sunshine, eager to rejoin the free world. He had to learn how to use a cellphone and adjust to modern life after a generation behind bars. Now he gives inspirational speeches and shows his work in a gallery, most recently in New York.'
b"Dixon says he's not bitter. His mother, though, still bristles when the subject of his incarceration comes up. He was imprisoned on her birthday, and she refused to celebrate any of them for the next 27 years."
b'Dixon and Adler came to the Masters to complete their journey in the place it really began. His art brought him here, just as it freed him from prison.'
b'"The artwork, it\'s like God was speaking to my soul," Dixon said. "He was just saying you know it\'s gonna be all right, you hang in there."'

b'WASHINGTON \xe2\x80\x94 U.S. President Donald Trump on Monday said he would award Tiger Woods the Presidential Medal of Freedom after the golfer won the Masters for the fifth time on Sunday.'
b'"Spoke to @TigerWoods to congratulate him on the great victory he had in yesterday\xe2\x80\x99s @TheMasters, & to inform him that because of his incredible Success & Comeback in Sports (Golf) and, more importantly, LIFE, I will be presenting him with the PRESIDENTIAL MEDAL OF FREEDOM," Trump tweeted.'
b'The victory on Sunday was one of the greatest comebacks in sports history, as the 43-year-old ended an 11-year major title drought having overcome personal and professional setbacks including a highly-public divorce and multiple surgeries. '
b'The one-stroke win at Augusta National led to an outpouring of support from sports greats and politicians including Trump.'
b'Trump, an avid golfer, and Woods have played together in the past including in February when the pair joined golf great Jack Nicklaus for a round at Trump National Golf Club in Jupiter, Florida. '
b"Trump appeared to follow the action at this year's Masters closely, tweeting well-wishes to the field on Saturday and encouraging people to tune in when Woods had the lead with just two holes left to play on Sunday. "
b'"Congratulations to @TigerWoods, a truly Great Champion!" Trump tweeted shortly after Woods sank a short putt to secure his 15th major title. '
b'"Love people who are great under pressure. What a fantastic life comeback for a really great guy!" he added later.'
b'The medal is the highest civilian honor in the United States and is given annually to people who have made outstanding contributions to the security or national interests of the country, to world peace, or to cultural or other significant public or private endeavors.'
b'Since taking office Trump has given the award to several athletes including former professional NFL players Roger Staubach and Alan Page and late professional baseball player George Herman "Babe" Ruth, Jr.'

b'By Reuters'
b"AUGUSTA, Georgia \xe2\x80\x94 With the successful staging of the Augusta National Women's Amateur on Saturday, the home of the Masters removed a little more of the stain left by decades of gender discrimination."
b"But more polish will be needed if one of the world's most exclusive clubs hopes to clean the slate entirely."
b'"You are now part of history of Augusta National along with all the great Masters champions who have been right here in this Butler Cabin," said Augusta National chairman Fred Ridley as he presented the winner\'s trophy to Jennifer Kupcho.'
b'The fact is, however, that women have long been a part of the history of Augusta National, albeit the dark chapter of exclusion.'
b"Founded by Bobby Jones and Clifford Roberts and opened for play in January 1933, Augusta National was a private sanctuary for some of the world's most powerful white men and for decades immune to outside influences and pressures."
b'Ron Townsend became the first African-American member in 1990 but it would be another two decades before women were admitted with former U.S. Secretary of State Condoleezza Rice and financier Darla Moore allowed through the doors in 2012.'
b'While the pace remains glacial, change has nonetheless crept into the Augusta DNA.'
b'Club membership is top secret but it is believed that four to six of the 300 or so members are women and have one of the iconic green jackets hanging in their lockers.'
b"Augusta National also hosts the hugely popular Drive, Chip and Putt Championship for both boys and girls and has now put its name and branding muscle to a women's tournament."
b'The images of women competing at a club where they had previously been denied entry was a powerful one that was universally applauded. '
b'Some, like activist Martha Burk, who in 2003 led a protest against Augusta National\'s men only policy, remain skeptical. She described the event as a "baby step" and "tokenism".'
b'Certainly it was an emotional day for golfing greats Nancy Lopez, Pak Se-ri, Lorena Ochoa and Annika Sorenstam, who took part in a ceremonial tee shot then watched as 30 young women seized an opportunity that had never been open to them.'
b'"When we were talking I was tearing up," said Lopez. "I was trying to hold back tears because there\'s so much pride involved in this.'
b'"It was just a tremendous feeling to be there and represent amateur golf, professional golf and what golf stands for here at Augusta National."'
b'"GREAT MOTIVATION"'
b'There was no downplaying the significance of the moment for Lorena Ochoa, who compared it to golf being played at the Olympics.'
b'"It\'s going to be a great motivation for the new generations," she said. '
b'"This is as big as a tournament that you have in your mind -- the U.S. Amateur, or the Olympics -- that you dream that you want to win."'
b'Without the Augusta National name attached to it, a tournament of this type would have been one watched by no more than a handful of family and friends.'
b"Instead women's amateur golf on Saturday found itself in the sporting spotlight."
b'The final round was broadcast live on national television and a gallery worthy of a major tournament descended on the course to witness a bit of history.'
b"While the golfing world was all but silent in 2003 when Burk was pushing for change, top men's players were squarely behind the women on Saturday."
b'Masters champion Bubba Watson, wearing his green jacket, watched from the first tee, while others like Rory McIlroy and Jack Nicklaus offered support on social media.'
b"While Augusta has put its name to the tournament, only one round was played at the iconic course and the question remains as to what happens next for women's golf and Augusta National."
b'"This is an historic moment, and hopefully they will continue to carry the torch, and who knows what opportunities will come 10, 15 years from now," said Sorenstam. "This is just the beginning. '
b'"We are trying to increase the interest in the game of golf, and tournaments like this will certainly do it. '
b'"I\'ve never seen so much exposure for a tournament, and to see these girls come up here and step it up and have so much fun and enjoy it, I mean, this is a dream come true."'
b' (Editing by Nick Mulvenney)'

b'"How can you compare Tiger Woods to Jack Nicklaus? It\'s not fair. Let him (Nicklaus) play today with these greens and raked bunkers or bunkers all the same width, and with a driver and a ball that goes 50 yards further," Player told reporters.'
b'Sam Snead was the most athletic, Ben Hogan the greatest golfer "tee-to-green" and Woods is perhaps the most talented, Player said. '

b'That is not to say the South African was not giving the most recognizable player in modern golf his due.'

b'Eddie Pepperell, who started Sunday six strokes behind McIlroy, caught him, and so, fleetingly, did Jhonattan Vegas, who also began the round six behind him. Down the stretch, Jim Furyk, who came from four back, inched ahead.'
b'In contrast to last year, when Webb Simpson squeezed all the drama from the finish with a four-stroke victory, Sunday was a knock-down-drag-out race to the wire, with eight players holding at least a share of the lead \xe2\x80\x94 including Vegas for 16 seconds \xe2\x80\x94 before McIlroy took command.'
b'McIlroy did not panic when he carded a double bogey on the fourth hole and made the turn in a one-over-par 37. b'McIlroy, of Northern Ireland, finished at 16-under 272, one ahead of Furyk, who closed with a 67, and two in front of Pepperell (66) and Vegas (66). Rahm struggled to a 76 and ended up in a four-way tie for 12th at 11 under.'

b'Furyk, who lives a short drive from the course, was one of the last players to earn his way into the field, and though he came up short in his bid for his first tour title since 2015, he had few complaints; the runner-up finish was his best showing in 23 starts in the event.'

b"(Reuters) - CBS Corp said on Tuesday that the broadcast of the Masters final round live coverage averaged 10.8 million viewers, making it the most-watched golf broadcast since last year's Masters final round. "
b"The final 18 holes, in which Tiger Woods came from behind to win his first major title in 11 years, was watched by 37.2 million viewers in total, up 41 percent from last year's live coverage. It was the most watched Masters Sunday in six years."
b'The victory led to an outpouring of praise from world leaders and U.S. President Donald Trump said he would award Tiger Woods the Presidential Medal of Freedom.'
b'Broadcast of the live coverage of the final round was moved to Sunday morning due to weather, which affected its ratings. The match was the most-watched morning golf game in 32 years. '

b'By The Associated Press'
b"The not-quite-ready-for-prime-time Thanksgiving exhibition with Tiger Woods and Phil Mickelson produced such bad golf that Mickelson and country singer Jake Owen traded barbs about it a day later at Jordan Spieth's wedding."
b'Owen said it was so bad he deserved a refund. He told Barstool Sports\' "Fore Play" podcast that Mickelson, who won $9 million from the TV spectacle, pulled out a wad of $100 bills, handed one to Owen and told him he had 90,000 more where that came from.'
b"Golf's two biggest attractions are back at the Masters, eager to play the kind of golf this week that they couldn't produce in The Match. The two 40-somethings will be on prominent display, though the trash talk that was promised on the pay-per-view money grab will not be heard on the hallowed grounds of Augusta National."
b'And, unlike The Match, the Masters will deliver.'
b'It always has, with moments like Woods stunning the field in a runaway victory at the age of 21, or Mickelson leaping for joy on the 18th green after finally winning his first major in 2004.'
b'It always has, even when an unknown like Danny Willett came from nowhere to win, only to quickly disappear from the golf landscape.'
b'And it even did last year when Patrick Reed won a green jacket that few in the Sunday crowd seemed particularly happy about.'
b'The Masters enjoys special status as the enduring annual rite of spring, the place every duffer who has ever picked up a club dreams of hitting shots. Set under magnificently manicured fairways and greens and framed by towering pines, it offers a tantalizing glimpse of summer in a place where nothing seems to change but something is different every year.'
b'Arnold Palmer won there four times and Jack Nicklaus six. Woods has four green jackets, and Mickelson has three.'
b"Still, the defending champion is rarely the focus and for the most part the big names in the game aren't either. The course is the star, even when the real tournament begins \xe2\x80\x94 as is Masters lore \xe2\x80\x94 on the back nine on Sunday."
b"That's true more than ever this year, even as spectators and television viewers got a rare sneak preview of Augusta National on Saturday for the first time with the final round of a women's amateur tournament."
b'Reed comes in mired in a deep slump that had him seeking the aid of swing coach David Leadbetter last month, at the insistence of his wife. Bookies in Las Vegas make him a 40-1 pick, long odds for someone trying to become the fourth player to repeat as Masters champion.'
b"Still, Reed said last month he was looking forward to everything about the Masters, except the fact he will have to turn in his green jacket if he's not successful in repeating."
b'"You want to keep it around as long as you can," Reed said of the famous jacket. "The only way you\'re going to do that is continue winning at Augusta and continue winning the event so you can have it year in and year out."'
b"History suggests that won't be happening, since only three players before Reed have returned to successfully defend their title. But there is golf to be played before that's decided, and a champion's dinner to be eaten."
b"Reed said at The Player's Championship that he figured out the menu for the dinner long before he won."
b'"Oh, I knew that back when I was 13," he said. "I mean, it was always a bone-in ribeye, mac and cheese, creamed corn, creamed spinach. I\'m going to fatten those boys up a little bit."'
b"Reed didn't exactly bask in the love of the galleries last year when he rolled in a 3-footer on the 18th green to beat Rickie Fowler by a shot and Spieth by two. The stories that followed didn't make him any easier to root for, when he declined to discuss why his parents weren't welcomed at the tournament despite living just a few miles away."
b"Mickelson and Woods, meanwhile, have had their own personal issues, though that hasn't dented their popularity. The two are icons of modern golf, and even in their 40s they are among the group of favorites that include Fowler, Spieth, Rory McIlroy and Dustin Johnson."
b"Just don't expect Mickelson to do what he did at the U.S. Open last year and run after a putt and hit it while it's still moving. Do that at Augusta National and you'd get a one-way trip back out Magnolia Lane, and no invitation in the mail the next spring."
b"Don't expect Mickelson or Woods to play as badly as they did in their pay-per-view match, either. Both know every inch of grass on Augusta National, both know how to hit miracle shots when it really matters and both have lots of experience in putting the green jacket on."
b"Then again, Woods hasn't won a Masters in 14 years, and Mickelson is almost a decade removed from his last green jacket. They're legends on a legendary golf course, but there are probably 20 younger players who can beat them when playing their best."
b'Mickelson and Woods sold their Thanksgiving match with a promise of riveting golf and even better TV.'
b"No need to sell this. It's the Masters, and it's as real as golf gets."

b'RANCHO MIRAGE, Calif. \xe2\x80\x94 Let other players take dead aim at titles and trophies. Jin Young Ko is finding success by directing her focus elsewhere.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI want to be the happiest player on the golf course,\xe2\x80\x9d Ko said.'
b'Ko, the latest star in South Korea\xe2\x80\x99s bright constellation, burst into tears Sunday after closing with a two-under-par 70 to win the ANA Inspiration. It was her second L.P.G.A. title in less than a month and her first major championship.'
b'Ko, who posted a 72-hole total of 10-under 278, finished three strokes ahead of her compatriot Mi Hyang Lee, who carded a final-round 70. Lexi Thompson, a former champion, shot a 67 for third, four strokes back.'
b'For Ko, 23, happiness was a 15-foot birdie putt on the 72nd hole, after which she collapsed into the embrace of her caddie, David Brooker, who has guided three players to this championship.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are a really good team,\xe2\x80\x9d Ko said.'
b'Ko capped her win by leaping into Poppie\xe2\x80\x99s Pond with Brooker by her side.'
b'Brooker said he was approached last year by an intermediary sent to gauge his interest in caddying for Ko. Brooker had worked with golfers who had played competitive rounds with her, so he had seen Ko\xe2\x80\x99s game up close and was impressed with her driving accuracy and self-possession.'
b'But he had an agreement to work for Paula Creamer, a 12-time winner worldwide, through the end of last season, her 14th as a professional. At the end of 2018, after Ko was named the L.P.G.A.\xe2\x80\x99s top rookie, Brooker made the switch.'
b'In her first six starts with Brooker on her bag, Ko has five top-3 finishes, including two victories. Her final-round scoring average is 66.83 strokes. It is a tossup as to who is the hottest player on the planet: Ko or the men\xe2\x80\x99s world No. 3, Rory McIlroy, who has seven top-9 finishes, including one victory, in seven starts in 2019.'
b'The 23-year-old Ko could not have asked for a more capable Sherpa than Brooker to help her plant her name at the top of the ANA Inspiration leader board. He entered the week having made 16 caddie appearances since 1997 at Mission Hills Country Club and two celebratory leaps into Poppie\xe2\x80\x99s Pond, with Grace Park in 2004 and Lorena Ochoa in 2008.'
b'Brooker knows the greens like his backyard, which is why Ko trusted him to read many of her putts.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cHe helps me all the time on the green or the fairways,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'Brooker\xe2\x80\x99s guidance can be more subtle. After Ko played in the afternoon Friday and signed for a 71, she said she wanted to spend what little daylight remained working on her swing. Brooker talked her out of it, explaining that the gusting wind would make any range work counterproductive.'
b'He suggested that she spend the time instead on her main area of emphasis during the off-season: chipping and putting.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe are really good team,\xe2\x80\x9d Ko said.'
b'Ko has four L.P.G.A. titles \xe2\x80\x94 and 14 over all \xe2\x80\x94 since she turned pro in 2013. Before earning her L.P.G.A. membership, Ko starred on the Korean L.P.G.A. tour. She was playing on her homeland circuit in 2015 when she took a three-stroke lead into the final round of her first major start, the Women\xe2\x80\x99s British Open.'
b'Ko, then 19, finished second to her compatriot Inbee Park.'
b'And though that runner-up finish offered validation that her game stacked up well against the best, she said last year that she was hesitant to jump headlong to the L.P.G.A.'
b'Before a tournament in Seoul last October, Ko said she engaged in considerable \xe2\x80\x9csoul searching\xe2\x80\x9d before she decided to leave home to compete on the American-based tour. Unlike many of her countrywomen, Ko does not maintain a residence in the United States.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe doesn\xe2\x80\x99t want a base over here,\xe2\x80\x9d Brooker said.'
b'Ko\xe2\x80\x99s homing instincts remind him of Ochoa, who was the women\xe2\x80\x99s world No. 1 when she retired at 28 because she could no longer bear to be apart from her family and away from her native Mexico for long stretches.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t think she\xe2\x80\x99s going to have one of those 20-year careers,\xe2\x80\x9d Brooker said. \xe2\x80\x9cI could see her playing out here five or six years and then retiring to have a family. She is not motivated by money, she\xe2\x80\x99s not motivated by titles. She just wants to have fun.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Ko can find the hilarity in courting disaster. On Saturday, she began the day four strokes off the lead, raced to a five-stroke advantage after 10 holes, then gave most of it back with a double bogey at No. 14 and a bogey at No. 15. After she used a pitching wedge to hit her tee shot into the water at the par-3 14th, Ko playfully rested her head on Brooker\xe2\x80\x99s shoulder, sighed and said, \xe2\x80\x9cOh, what have I done?\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Her third-round wobble proved instructive for Ko, who kept calm when she smelled the whiff of disaster on her back nine Sunday. After bogeys on the 13th and 15th holes whittled her lead over Lee to a single stroke, Ko rebounded with a birdie on the par-3 16th to give herself breathing room.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cShe is just so smart for her age,\xe2\x80\x9d Brooker, said. \xe2\x80\x9cShe knows what she\xe2\x80\x99s doing out there.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'AUGUSTA Ga. (Reuters) - Tony Finau is no stranger to making a charge at Augusta National, fortunately for him the one he made at the Masters on Saturday left him with a better chance of slipping into a Green Jacket than an ankle brace.'
b"Finau, who dislocated his ankle while celebrating an ace in last year's Par-3 Contest on the eve of his Masters debut, surged into contention with an eight-under 64 that brought him to 11 under, two shots off leader Francesco Molinari."
b"His also tied the tournament's front-nine record with a six-under 30. "
b'"I can attack the golf course if I\'m hitting my driver well, and I have been thus far. I felt good," said Finau. "Going into today, I felt calm and comfortable, and I think my score showed that."'
b"While Finau courageously finished in a share of 10th place at last year's Masters, he was still largely known as the golfer who blew out his ankle while celebrating a hole-in-one."
b'Finau even had some fun at his own expense this week, sending the gallery into fits of laughter when he put on a hilariously high-topped shoe featuring added support for his since-healed ankle before teeing off in the Par-3 Contest.'
b'Finau, who started the day four shots back of the co-leaders, got off to a scorching start on Saturday, opening with three consecutive birdies.'
b'From there he was off to the races, adding another birdie at the sixth before making eagle at the par-five eighth after his approach settled eight inches from the cup.'
b'Finau, the first golfer of Tongan and American Samoan descent to play on the PGA Tour, added another two birdies on the back nine.'
b'The 29-year-old American will play in the final threesome on Sunday with Molinari (66) and Tiger Woods (67). '
b'With heavy rain and thunderstorms forecast for late on Sunday, officials have decided to send golfers off in threesomes from both the first and 10th tees rather than the traditional pairs in an attempt to get the final round completed.'
b"Finau is no stranger to being in contention at one of golf's blue-riband events having been in the mix on the final day of last year's U.S. Open, a learning experience he hopes will pay off of Sunday."
b'"It\'s going to help because I\'ve been in that\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x91\xe2\x80\x91 I\'ve been in that situation before," said Finau. "Last year I had the lead going into the final round of the U.S. Open, and I took a run at it toward the end.'
b'"I feel like I\'ve learned some things about that finish that I can apply to tomorrow, and hopefully do better."'

b'By Karen Crouse'
b'AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 Tiger Woods completed a comeback from personal and professional adversity on Sunday, capturing his fifth Masters title and his 15th major tournament with a victory that snapped a decade-long championship drought and instantly returned him to the top of the sports world.'
b'It was a monumental triumph for Woods, a come-from-behind victory for a player who had had so much go wrong on the course and off after his personal life began to come apart on Thanksgiving night in 2009.'
b'As such, it was only fitting that after he walked off the 18th hole on Sunday, his one-stroke victory secure, his path to the official scoring office was gridlocked with well-wishers, including many of the golfers he vanquished over four grueling days at Augusta National Golf Club.'
b'Woods triumphed in almost stoic fashion, playing with shrewdness and determination over the final stretch of holes while the other players who were grouped with him on the leaderboard took turns succumbing to the pressure of trying to win the Masters.'
b'And although Woods did bogey the final hole, he did so with a two-stroke lead, victory in sight and the knowledge that he could give one of those strokes back and still win the tournament.'
b'Only when he tapped in his final putt did Woods let loose with a joyous shout that revealed how much the victory meant to him.'
b'At 43, Woods became the second-oldest winner of the Masters, behind Jack Nicklaus, who won here in 1986 at age 46 and who holds the record for victories in major tournaments, 18. And Woods\xe2\x80\x99s victory immediately reverberated beyond golf and, for that matter, sports.'
b'The win even led to a rare moment of agreement between President Trump and former President Barack Obama. \xe2\x80\x9cWhat a fantastic life comeback for a really great guy!\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 the President said on Twitter. \xe2\x80\x9cTo come back and win the Masters after all the highs and lows is a testament to excellence, grit and determination,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 Obama posted.'
b'Francesco Molinari entered the final round of the Masters alone in the lead by two strokes at 13 under. He stayed atop the leaderboard by himself until the last group \xe2\x80\x94 Molinari,  Tiger Woods and Tony Finau \xe2\x80\x94 got to the 12th tee.  At which point, Molinari proceeded to double bogey the hole and set up a wild finish in which six golfers at one point or another held at least a share of the lead. (Woods, Molinari, Xander Schauffele, Patrick Cantlay, Brooks Koepka, Dustin Johnson). There was briefly a five-way tie for first until Woods took sole possession of the lead for good at the 15th hole, where he birdied and Molinari made another double bogey.'

b'By The New York Times'
b'[Just like the old days, Tiger Woods won the Masters by intimidating his opponents.]'
b'Woods\xe2\x80\x99s victory had an epic feel to it. At Augusta, on perhaps the sport\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stage, was its seminal figure, suddenly back on top, which is where he was a decade ago when everything suddenly went sideways for him.'
b'What followed was a long, painful period of his life, in which his body repeatedly broke down and his marriage collapsed. But after prevailing on Sunday, Woods is back in the pantheon of the sports world\xe2\x80\x99s biggest stars, back on a level with LeBron James, Serena Williams and Lionel Messi, back in a space he entered with his first Masters victory in 1997, when he was a skinny 21-year-old a year removed from Stanford who declared \xe2\x80\x9cHello World\xe2\x80\x9d in a classic Nike commercial.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s unreal for me to experience this,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 Woods said in a television interview after his victory on Sunday. \xe2\x80\x9cIt was one of the hardest I\xe2\x80\x99ve ever had to win just because of what\xe2\x80\x99s transpired the last couple of years.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'The long drought Woods endured between major championships \xe2\x80\x94 his previous one came at the 2008 United States Open \xe2\x80\x94 would have once seemed inconceivable. The same could be said for the 14 years it took for Woods to finally win his fifth title at Augusta National, a course so suited for his game that Nicklaus once predicted that Woods would collect more than the combined 10 Masters titles that he and Arnold Palmer won there.'
b'And yet there was an eerie familiarity to what took place on Sunday. Woods played his final round before crowds that were 10 to 12 deep for hundreds of yards at every hole \xe2\x80\x94 from tee box to green.'
b'In a sense, though, the gallery that really mattered to Woods was much smaller and consisted of his mother, Kultida, and his two children \xe2\x80\x94 his 10-year-old son, Charlie Axel, and his 11-year-old daughter, Sam Alexis. His children were among the first to greet him once his triumph was complete. Neither had been born when Woods basically ruled the sport.'
b'They essentially knew of their father\xe2\x80\x99s exploits from photographs and other people\xe2\x80\x99s memories \xe2\x80\x94 and they knew golf mostly as a game that had caused their father terrible distress. But not anymore.'
b'The years between Woods\xe2\x80\x99s 14th and 15th victories in major tournaments included an immense number of setbacks, although his struggles actually date to the 2006 death of his father, Earl, who was his soulmate and putting guru. Two years later, Woods won the United States Open victory on a left leg in need of surgery, but a year after that, a marital dispute about his philandering led to a car accident and a succession of lurid headlines. A divorce followed in 2010.'
b'Tiger Woods\xe2\x80\x99s record in the 11 years since his last victory in a major tournament.'

b'The ensuing years brought repeated back operations, which led to an addiction to painkillers and culminated in pain so searing that, before an operation in 2017, he questioned whether he could play professionally again. That year, he hit rock bottom when he was charged with driving under the influence after he was found in a painkiller haze at the wheel of his car with the motor running.'
b'Woods said that when he was down, he gained strength from what he described as his children\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9cinfectious happiness.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cTo have my kids here, it\xe2\x80\x99s come full circle,\xe2\x80\x9d he said after Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s final round. \xe2\x80\x9cMy dad was here in \xe2\x80\x9997, and now I\xe2\x80\x99m the dad with two kids there.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'With a closing round of two-under-par 70, Woods edged two other major champions \xe2\x80\x94 Dustin Johnson and Brooks Koepka \xe2\x80\x94 as well as Xander Schauffele, a 25-year-old from San Diego. Woods\xe2\x80\x99s 72-hole score of 13-under 275 was one shot better than his total in his 2005 victory at Augusta. And it was the first time that Woods, who started the day two strokes off the lead, had come from behind in the final round to win a major tournament.'
b'Woods\xe2\x80\x99s children were also with him last summer when he saw the first real glimmers of hope in his comeback \xe2\x80\x94 at the British Open. They saw him play his way into contention over the first three days of that tournament and then briefly take the lead in the final round on his way to a tie for sixth. Afterward, he told his children that he hoped that they were proud of how he fought and refused to give up.'
b'At Augusta, his children arrived on Saturday night, providing extra motivation for Woods to prevail. Parenthood has imbued Woods with extra patience, which came in handy on the front nine on Sunday, when he made back-to-back bogeys while elsewhere on the course players were leapfrogging over one another and into contention with birdies and eagles. Indeed, late in Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s round, 10 players, including Woods, were within two strokes of the lead.'
b'But amid that intense grouping, it was Woods who found a way to finish first.'
b'Woods\xe2\x80\x99s first Masters title, in 1997, by an astounding 12 strokes, left an indelible mark on the sport. He became the first African-American \xe2\x80\x94 Woods is also half Thai \xe2\x80\x94 to win golf\xe2\x80\x99s most exalted championship. He reshaped the game, making it more athletic and more popular \xe2\x80\x94 especially outside the United States.'
b'In 1997, the first person at Augusta to greet Woods as he came off the final hole in triumph was his father, whose grand plan Woods had realized with his victory. His mother was there, too. She was also on hand Sunday, but after her embrace, Woods took a few steps forward and was smothered by his second family \xe2\x80\x94 the other players, some of whom were almost young enough to be his children.'
b'Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s final round was moved up five hours to avoid an ominous forecast for later in the day. Players were grouped in threesomes to speed play. Woods took the lead for good on the par 5 15th hole with a birdie putt. And when he then arrived at the 16th tee, a familiar face and friend \xe2\x80\x94 the record-setting swimmer Michael Phelps \xe2\x80\x94 was standing close enough to touch him.'
b'It was Phelps who had spent two months in a treatment center in 2014 after trying to self-medicate with alcohol. It was Phelps who became an informal counselor to Woods after the 2017 painkiller episode. And it was Phelps who was on hand as Woods closed out his comeback with his final putt.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen I tapped the putt in \xe2\x80\x94 I don\xe2\x80\x99t know what I did,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x99 Woods said. \xe2\x80\x9cI know I screamed.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'And as he then put on the winner\xe2\x80\x99s green jacket for a fifth time, he said something everyone knew but might have forgotten: \xe2\x80\x9cIt fits.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'(Reuters) - A Wisconsin man who bet $85,000 on Tiger Woods to win the Masters was handed a check for $1.275 million by bookmaker William Hill on Monday.'
b'A day after Woods came from behind to win his first major title in 11 years, a video circulating online showed James Adducci picking up his check at SLS Las Vegas Hotel & Casino.'
b'The 39-year-old told Golf Digest that the 14-1 bet was his first sports wager. The stockbroker, who works from home, said he planned to spend the winnings on home improvements and paying off debts while investing the rest. '
b"Reports said the net $1.19 million payout was the largest for a single ticket golf bet in the company's history in the United States. "
b'"Pretty good first bet," Nick Bogdanovich, William Hill\'s U.S. director of trading, told ESPN. '
b'"It\'s great to see Tiger back. It\'s a painful day for William Hill -- our biggest loss ever -- but a great day for golf." '
b'William Hill was not the only bookmaker to feel the pain after the 43-year-old Woods secured his fifth green jacket at Augusta National. '

b"AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 Golf's not-so-mad scientist Bryson DeChambeau has been putting with the flagstick in the hole for much of this year after a rule change that allowed it."
b'Perhaps it is too bad he did not remove the stick for his 195-yard approach shot to the final hole at Augusta National on Thursday.'
b'Had he so, the ball might have gone in, but instead it clattered against the stick and stopped a couple of inches away for a tap-in birdie.'
b'"Should have pulled the flagstick out," the American joked after a six-under-par 66 that tied for the first-round lead with Ryder Cup team mate Brooks Koepka.'
b'"But no, it was a great shot, and I was excited just to tap-in to finish off a great round."'
b'It was his first sub-70 score in nine rounds at Augusta, where he tied for 21st and 38th in his previous appearances.'
b'Physics major DeChambeau has brought a level of scientific analysis to golf perhaps unmatched by a professional.'
b'The 25-year-old former U.S. Amateur champion plays with shafts of all his irons the same length, all but unheard of until he burst onto the scene. He claims it allows for a more repeatable swing plane.'
b'He knows that it will take a few more rides at the rodeo to learn every nuance of Augusta, where experience does not go astray.'
b'"I don\'t know if I\'m going to be able to figure out every little nuance of this golf course in my third year playing, but what I can do is prepare as good as I can and be comfortable with my own game in any situation," he said.'
b'"So that when I get out here, any situation that arises, I feel I can execute and play the game that\'s necessary."'
b'Only one under after 11 holes, there was little to suggest the fireworks to come.'
b'"Executed a beautiful nine-iron on 12 that got me rolling," said DeChambeau, who also birdied the final four holes.'
b'"What a magical back nine.'
b'"I was hitting it great all day, driving it well, just an accumulation of great golf that finally showed in the score."'

b'By The Associated Press'
b'AUGUSTA, Ga. \xe2\x80\x94 The first green jacket was all about the future.'
b'The fifth green jacket Tiger Woods won Sunday at the Masters was more about the past, best measured by a powerful celebration and enormous popularity than by any ripple effect it might have in golf.'
b'Tim Finchem was in this third year as PGA Tour commissioner in 1997 when a 21-year-old Woods \xe2\x80\x94 in his 15th start on tour, already with three victories \xe2\x80\x94 set 20 records at Augusta National with a 12-shot victory that made him the youngest Masters champion.'
b'Finchem now is in his third year of retirement from the PGA Tour with his own green jacket as an Augusta National member. He was at the Masters most of the week until watching with millions of others on Sunday, with a different perspective from most.'
b'"It was eerie to me on Sunday because in my mind, this was just a \'97 repeat. It was incredible," Finchem said Tuesday. "But then I started thinking about it, and it\'s not that at all. It was very different."'
b'Woods was the freight train everyone heard coming in 1997.'
b'The most dominant junior ever, he won three straight U.S. Junior Amateurs and three straight U.S. Amateurs. The last one was held the same week as the World Series of Golf at Firestone, and Finchem once recalled how players would watch the U.S. Amateur in the locker room and wonder what they were in for when Woods turned pro.'
b'Within two months, Woods qualified for the Tour Championship by winning twice in seven starts. He won the Tournament of Champions to start the next year. And then he demolished the field and Augusta National like no one had ever seen, making him the first man of color in a green jacket.'
b'It remains his most significant victory because it changed the entire golf landscape.'
b'"Golf fans were all into him," Finchem said. "But they hadn\'t seen that much of him except for winning tournaments."'
b'Now they know a lot more \xe2\x80\x94 too much, at times.'
b"It's those 22 years between his first and latest major that make No. 15 the most popular of all."
b'"Between then and now, these people have watched his every move \xe2\x80\x94 every difficult challenge, losing his game, coming back, private issues \xe2\x80\x94 and so they know a lot more about him as a person," Finchem said. "People are just over the moon about this. Part of this has to do with how he\'s handled himself the last two, three, four years. He\'s been a very positive force, a leader among the players, and he\'s at another level of interface with millions and millions of fans.'
b'"They love to watch him play golf."'
b"That much hasn't changed."
b"Television ratings spiked following that 1997 victory, right when the PGA Tour was negotiating a new television contract. The total prize money on the PGA Tour in 1997 was $70.7 million, and it jumped to $135.8 million under the new TV deal in 1999. This year it's at $340 million, not including FedEx Cup bonus money."
b'Woods made everyone rich.'
b'Ratings still spike whenever he plays. Galleries are larger and louder.'
b"It's been that way since 1997, even during the lean years for Woods when his image was tarnished through tabloid stories of extramarital affairs, when his body began to break down and his glutes didn't activate, when he returned too soon from his first back surgery and went five years without winning."
b'The appeal never left. When he plays, people want to watch.'
b"When he wasn't playing \xe2\x80\x94 Woods went two straight years without a tee time in the majors \xe2\x80\x94 the legend grew because all anyone had were memories, and those were far more powerful than anything he showed on the golf course."
b"That's why his latest Masters victory was so amazing to so many."
b'Memories became real. The Sunday red shirt was brighter than ever. There was audible excitement in the press building, from a younger generation that had never seen him win a major, from an older generation that thought it might never happen again.'
b'It felt for a moment that nothing had changed, when so much has.'
b'And in some respects, that makes it even bigger.'
b'Woods no longer is invincible. This was his hardest major to win, and not just because he had overcome so much in his life and with his health. Woods had never won a major when so many others had a chance on the back nine.'
b'He won because he hit better shots, smarter shots. This was more about execution than mystique.'
b'And it was about redemption.'
b'Finchem recalled one other moment, at Torrey Pines in 2015 a week after Woods shot 82 in the Phoenix Open, when he was asked if he was worried about Woods.'
b'There was concern as a fan because Finchem wanted to see him at his best as he challenged the records for majors (Jack Nicklaus) and career PGA Tour wins (Sam Snead). As a commissioner? Not so much, because everyone was watching.'
b'"But now, it occurred to me looking back on it that in many ways, people love to watch him play golf, but they wanted to love him," Finchem said.'
b"They missed him. Now they have him back, and for how much longer doesn't matter as much as it once did."

b'By Lisa D. Mickey'
b'Minimizing manicured grass isn\xe2\x80\x99t the first thing that comes to mind when you think of improvements to a high-end golf course.'
b'But Sailfish Point Golf Club on Hutchinson Island on Florida\xe2\x80\x99s east coast, did just that. Now, butterflies have moved in where native grasses and flowers have been allowed to grow tall.'
b'Across the state, on Sanibel Island, the Sanctuary Golf Club ripped out concrete cart paths and brought in beehives to help pollinate the local wildflowers.'
b'In Skidaway, Ga., near Savannah, the Landings Club dug a new irrigation system to lower water consumption, and it built nesting areas for a native terrapin rescue program.'
b'Golf courses and environmental initiatives haven\xe2\x80\x99t always coexisted. But today, many course superintendents \xe2\x80\x94 the men and women who plan and maintain courses \xe2\x80\x94 hope to reshape that thinking.'
b'Sustainability efforts are often \xe2\x80\x9cmotivated by economics,\xe2\x80\x9d said Max Adler, the editorial director of Golf Digest. \xe2\x80\x9cThe whole industry is seeing a correction away from the very manicured, overmanufactured look of golf\xe2\x80\x94and at the same time what really motivates golf courses to pursue that look is the bottom line. The less water you use, the less grass grows, the less maintenance you have to cover.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In the last 10 years, he said, many clubs have replaced manicured areas of their courses \xe2\x80\x9cwith sand, with native floras and shrubs that exist naturally on the topography and just leave it. And it looks beautiful.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you\xe2\x80\x99re doing things that are economically sound, it\xe2\x80\x99s often in line with what you are doing environmentally,\xe2\x80\x9d said James Murphy, an extension specialist in turf management at Rutgers University in New Jersey.'
b'Players and residents also are demanding more eco-friendly practices.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s very important to people now that the community they live in respects the environment and takes care of it,\xe2\x80\x9d said Kristen Cheskaty, a broker and a managing partner at Sailfish Point Realty in Stuart, Fla.'
b'Because of that, golf communities in the United States and elsewhere in the world are focusing on things as varied as eliminating plastic and foam cups in their snack shops and reducing fertilizers and chemicals in the upkeep of the fairways.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cAll the little things add up,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Adler said. \xe2\x80\x9cEven though it\xe2\x80\x99s a small footprint for the day, over the course of the season it\xe2\x80\x99s real. More importantly it sends a message to people\xe2\x80\x99s minds that we want to be thoughtful and sensitive to the environment.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Florida\xe2\x80\x99s Sailfish Point has followed guidelines created by a not-for-profit environmental education organization called Audubon International, which offers a certification program for good golf-course management practices.'
b'Sailfish Point \xe2\x80\x94 a private 532-acre waterfront development with 520 low-rise homes, condominiums and townhouses \xe2\x80\x94 is bordered on the east by the Atlantic Ocean, the Fort Pierce Inlet to the north, and the Indian River Lagoon to the west.'
b'But in recent years, the lagoon has suffered from extensive algae blooms that most experts believe are related to discharge from Lake Okeechobeee, which is surrounded by farmland and polluted by fertilizer runoff.'
b'Scott MacPhee, the director of golf course operations at Sailfish Point, said many residents were concerned about any role the golf course could play in contributing to such pollution.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cA lot of fingers could easily be pointed at our community and our operation, and I didn\xe2\x80\x99t want that for our members,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. MacPhee said. \xe2\x80\x9cWhether the blame is on golf courses, farms or septic tanks, ultimately, we all want to do the right thing and we all want clean water.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'More than 800 golf courses in the United States and 2,100 courses in 34 countries have been certified by Audubon International.'
b'At Sailfish Point, earning the certificate took about two years. The work began in 2016 and included an environmental assessment and developing a wildlife and habitat management plan; reducing chemical use; and stepping up water conservation. In some areas, the golf course staff planted vegetation buffer zones, allowing growth of mangrove trees and aquatic plants to form a barrier between the golf course and waterways.'
b'Mark Perry, the executive director at the Florida Oceanographic Society in Stuart, who has consulted with the staff at Sailfish Point, said that the development\xe2\x80\x99s buffer zones are \xe2\x80\x9cgood common practice to let the shoreline vegetation help absorb nutrients\xe2\x80\x9d that can be damaging to the environment.'
b'Although Audubon International began the certification program around 30 years ago, a degree of confusion still exists about its relationship with the 114-year-old National Audubon Society, a nonprofit conservation group with the mission \xe2\x80\x9cto protect birds and the places they need, today and tomorrow.\xe2\x80\x9d The two are separate, unrelated entities.'
b'In Georgia, Chris Steigelman, who oversees three of the six Audubon International-certified golf courses at the Landings, said the certification process included installing a more drought-tolerant turf grass with a deeper root zone and a more effective irrigation system, which cost more than $10 million. Those steps have enabled the Landings to reduce water use by nearly 40 percent on its courses, he said.'
b'The Landings, situated within tidal salt marshes and the Atlantic Intracoastal Waterway, is also popular with native Diamondback Terrapins, which had a risky habit of depositing their eggs in golf course bunkers.'
b'Carolyn McInerney, a local real estate agent who lives at the Landings, began the Diamondback Terrapin Rescue Project by placing the eggs in little flower pots on her back porch.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cNow, we have five different nest boxes built around the golf course with community signs telling people about the program, as well as terrapin hatchling release parties,\xe2\x80\x9d Mr. Steigelman said. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s become a big community project.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In addition to the terrapin nests, the Landings has a system of bluebird boxes installed throughout its courses, monitored by community volunteers; pollinator gardens with native plantings for bees and butterflies; and a bird-cam to monitor owl, eagle and osprey nesting.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cPeople are looking for quality of life and that truly sells the island,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. McInerney said. \xe2\x80\x9cMore and more people are interested in nature.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Meredith Welch moved to Skidaway Island in 2008 after working for 20 years in New York City. She said she had been attracted to a place where she could be outdoors all year'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWhen I became a resident here, I couldn\xe2\x80\x99t believe I could sit in my backyard and watch hawks, fox, deer and an amazing parade of animals walk through because there are no fences between neighbors,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'
b'After seeing the benefits of certification for the golf courses at the Landing, Ms. Welch helped start an effort to get Audubon certification for the city\xe2\x80\x99s residential section, a process that took five years.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have a right to clean water and clean air,\xe2\x80\x9d Ms. Welch said. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd we can learn that we should protect things that are fragile and precious.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'In southwest Florida, the Sanctuary stands out for its location.'
b'The community and its course, which has been certified by Audubon International, are surrounded by the 6,300-acre J.N. Ding Darling National Wildlife Refuge \xe2\x80\x94 home to more than 300 species of birds, 50 species of reptiles and more than 30 mammal species. Two-thirds of the island is protected land.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you\xe2\x80\x99re going to be buying real estate on Sanibel Island, you\xe2\x80\x99ve already bought into the environmental side of things and you probably already get it,\xe2\x80\x9d said Kyle Sweet, the superintendent at the Sanctuary Golf Club, the island\xe2\x80\x99s only private course.'
b'Mr. Sweet not only maintains his course to Audubon International standards, but he also is guided by the wildlife refuge, as well as by rigid city requirements. Water quality and chemical nutrient loads are regularly monitored and the city issues an annual grade.'
b'Even residences are regulated in regard to impermeable surfaces, such as driveways. The Sanctuary has removed more than a mile and a half of concrete cart paths from the course.'
b'The course has also converted to hardier, salt-tolerant turf grass and upgraded its irrigation system for a 30 percent savings in water use.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cWe have a lot of members who are on the board at the Sanibel-Captiva Conservation Foundation and Ding Darling National Wildlife Refuge,\xe2\x80\x9d said Kathryn Riggio, the membership coordinator at the Sanctuary. \xe2\x80\x9cThey are very invested in our environmental responsibility.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'After Dr. Wendy Kindig, a Sanctuary resident and golf club member, retired from her clinical nephrology practice, she got involved in enviromental efforts at the Sanctuary, as well as on the board of the \xe2\x80\x9cDing\xe2\x80\x9d Darling Wildlife Society.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cConservation is pretty ingrained in this community,\xe2\x80\x9d she said.'

b'By Reuters'
b'AUGUSTA Ga. (Reuters) - With the cool stroke of a putter under ominous clouds hovering over the 18th green at Augusta National, Tiger Woods put an emphatic finishing touch on the most redemptive victory in sport history on Sunday.'
b'While the scene was a familiar one since Woods came into the week with four Green Jackets, this one was the most improbable given it followed years of surgeries and personal problems that convinced many the best golfer of his generation was done.'
b'But the 43-year-old Woods, who two years ago was barely hitting 60-yard shots as he worked his way back from spinal fusion surgery in April 2017, turned back the clock to deliver the sporting world a tale of redemption unlike any other.'
b'"I had serious doubts after what transpired a couple years ago. I could barely walk. I couldn\'t sit. Couldn\'t lay down. I really couldn\'t do much of anything," said Woods.'
b'"Luckily I had the procedure on my back, which gave me a chance at having a normal life. But then all of a sudden, I realized I could actually swing a golf club again.'
b'"I felt if I could somehow piece this together that I still had the hands to do it. The body\'s not the same as it was a long time ago, but I still have good hands."'
b'When his tap-in bogey settled in the cup for a one-shot win, Woods threw up his arms in triumph, igniting chants of "Tiger Tiger" that bounced through the pines as he went on to share celebratory hugs with his mother, two children and girlfriend.'
b'The moment was a long time coming for the former world number one, who last tasted major success at the 2008 U.S. Open when his oldest child, daughter Sam, was still an infant.'
b'Since that day, Woods went through a highly-public divorce in 2010 after revelations of his marital infidelities convinced him to take a self-imposed hiatus from professional golf, a DUI arrest in 2017 as well as multiple knee and back surgeries.'
b"'STRUGGLED FOR YEARS'"
b"Ever since Woods appeared on television's Mike Douglas Show at the age of two displaying his raw putting skills alongside Bob Hope, he has been expected to produce the remarkable."
b'And while the list of remarkable feats that Woods went on to achieve on the golf course is seemingly never ending, even he admitted this triumph, which drew congratulatory messages from U.S. President Donald Trump and former President Barack Obama, is among the most special.'
b'"It would be up there," Woods said when asked where his latest major ranks. "One of the hardest I have ever had to win just because what has transpired the last couple years with trying to come back to playing."'
b"Woods was two back of overnight leader Francesco Molinari when he stepped up to the par-four 11th, which marks the start of a five-hole stretch at Augusta National where the year's first major often hangs in the balance."
b"After yet another errant tee shot, Woods recovered with a skillful approach at 11 for par then moved into a share of the lead at the par-three 12th where Molinari made double-bogey after his tee shot went into Rae's Creek."
b'From there Woods, clad in his familiar final-round red shirt and black pants and the galleries hanging on his every swing, was off to the races as he showcased his competitive nerve to win a major for the first time while trailing after 54 holes. '
b'To do so, Woods had to fend off a slew of big-name players who at some point over the back nine either held a share of the lead or were just a shot back.'
b"Woods said one of the things he was most happy about was that his children, who were at last year's British Open when he could not hang onto a back-nine lead, were able to witness it in person after watching him fight pain for so long."
b'"The kids are starting to understand how much this game means to me, and some of the things I\'ve done in the game; prior to comeback, they only knew that golf caused me a lot of pain," said Woods.'
b'"If I tried to swing a club I would be on the ground and I struggled for years, and that\'s basically all they remember.'
b"With the win Woods broke Gary Player's record (13 years) for the longest gap between Masters wins. It also breathed new life into a decades-long debate about whether the 15-times major winner can catch Jack Nicklaus (18) on the all-time list."
b"When he finally slipped back into the winner's Green Jacket, a scene many golf fans had longed for but never thought they would see again, Woods had just two words to say:"
b'"It fits."'
b' (Reporting by Frank Pingue, editing by Pritha Sarkar)'
