b'By Reuters'
b'AUGUSTA Ga. (Reuters) - With the cool stroke of a putter under ominous clouds hovering over the 18th green at Augusta National, Tiger Woods put an emphatic finishing touch on the most redemptive victory in sport history on Sunday.'
b'While the scene was a familiar one since Woods came into the week with four Green Jackets, this one was the most improbable given it followed years of surgeries and personal problems that convinced many the best golfer of his generation was done.'
b'But the 43-year-old Woods, who two years ago was barely hitting 60-yard shots as he worked his way back from spinal fusion surgery in April 2017, turned back the clock to deliver the sporting world a tale of redemption unlike any other.'
b'"I had serious doubts after what transpired a couple years ago. I could barely walk. I couldn\'t sit. Couldn\'t lay down. I really couldn\'t do much of anything," said Woods.'
b'"Luckily I had the procedure on my back, which gave me a chance at having a normal life. But then all of a sudden, I realized I could actually swing a golf club again.'
b'"I felt if I could somehow piece this together that I still had the hands to do it. The body\'s not the same as it was a long time ago, but I still have good hands."'
b'When his tap-in bogey settled in the cup for a one-shot win, Woods threw up his arms in triumph, igniting chants of "Tiger Tiger" that bounced through the pines as he went on to share celebratory hugs with his mother, two children and girlfriend.'
b'The moment was a long time coming for the former world number one, who last tasted major success at the 2008 U.S. Open when his oldest child, daughter Sam, was still an infant.'
b'Since that day, Woods went through a highly-public divorce in 2010 after revelations of his marital infidelities convinced him to take a self-imposed hiatus from professional golf, a DUI arrest in 2017 as well as multiple knee and back surgeries.'
b"'STRUGGLED FOR YEARS'"
b"Ever since Woods appeared on television's Mike Douglas Show at the age of two displaying his raw putting skills alongside Bob Hope, he has been expected to produce the remarkable."
b'And while the list of remarkable feats that Woods went on to achieve on the golf course is seemingly never ending, even he admitted this triumph, which drew congratulatory messages from U.S. President Donald Trump and former President Barack Obama, is among the most special.'
b'"It would be up there," Woods said when asked where his latest major ranks. "One of the hardest I have ever had to win just because what has transpired the last couple years with trying to come back to playing."'
b"Woods was two back of overnight leader Francesco Molinari when he stepped up to the par-four 11th, which marks the start of a five-hole stretch at Augusta National where the year's first major often hangs in the balance."
b"After yet another errant tee shot, Woods recovered with a skillful approach at 11 for par then moved into a share of the lead at the par-three 12th where Molinari made double-bogey after his tee shot went into Rae's Creek."
b'From there Woods, clad in his familiar final-round red shirt and black pants and the galleries hanging on his every swing, was off to the races as he showcased his competitive nerve to win a major for the first time while trailing after 54 holes. '
b'To do so, Woods had to fend off a slew of big-name players who at some point over the back nine either held a share of the lead or were just a shot back.'
b"Woods said one of the things he was most happy about was that his children, who were at last year's British Open when he could not hang onto a back-nine lead, were able to witness it in person after watching him fight pain for so long."
b'"The kids are starting to understand how much this game means to me, and some of the things I\'ve done in the game; prior to comeback, they only knew that golf caused me a lot of pain," said Woods.'
b'"If I tried to swing a club I would be on the ground and I struggled for years, and that\'s basically all they remember.'
b"With the win Woods broke Gary Player's record (13 years) for the longest gap between Masters wins. It also breathed new life into a decades-long debate about whether the 15-times major winner can catch Jack Nicklaus (18) on the all-time list."
b"When he finally slipped back into the winner's Green Jacket, a scene many golf fans had longed for but never thought they would see again, Woods had just two words to say:"
b'"It fits."'
b' (Reporting by Frank Pingue, editing by Pritha Sarkar)'

b'On Golf'
b'By Bill Pennington'
b'The cheering was already raucous as Tiger Woods walked up the 18th fairway on Saturday, but when he smiled and tipped his cap, the volume doubled. The clamor diminished ever so slightly, and then Woods raised his putter in salute, and the roar reached new heights. A few strides later, Woods was on the green, and he offered a wave of his right hand and another grin. This time, the crowd erupted with its most thunderous ovation.'
b'It was hard to tell who was having more fun: the crowd as it shouted its welcome back or a playful Woods as he relished the sounds.'
b'One thing was certain: The reality of a breathtaking Tiger Woods Sunday at the Masters \xe2\x80\x94 the meaningful kind few expected to ever see again \xe2\x80\x94 was setting in for the fans at Augusta National Golf Club, and for sports fans everywhere. Woods ended his third round by tapping in for par and a five-under-par 67, good enough to get into Sunday\xe2\x80\x99s final threesome (a change from the usual pairs to speed things up ahead of expected bad weather). Woods will head into Augusta\xe2\x80\x99s typically dramatic fourth round just two strokes behind the leader, Francesco Molinari.'
b'[The drought is over. With a strong final round, Tiger Woods won The Masters.]'
b'But in the warmth of a spring Saturday evening, the throng around the 18th green did not want to let Woods go. He began to exit, but a last full-throated hurrah from the crowd caused Woods to turn back briefly \xe2\x80\x94 as if he wanted to save a mental image of the scene.'
b'Then, finally, he began the walk up the hill toward the clubhouse locker room.'
b'Still, fans surged anew to be near him, lining up 10 deep along the narrow path protected by ropes and security officials. Their voices followed and enveloped Woods like a cascading wave, cresting the rise as he did, and then flowing back down the other side of the knoll until Woods ducked his head inside a small white door and disappeared.'
b'Even without Woods to fete in person, the fans, some of them gleefully facing one another, continued to shout and cheer. It was as if they were celebrating their own good fortune.'
b'Tiger Woods, at 11 under for the tournament, was two strokes off the lead at the Masters with 18 holes to go. It was no time for quiet.'
b'[Read how Tiger Woods pushed his body to the point of breakdown and then came back.]'
b'Afterward, Woods conceded that he felt the ground-shaking decibel level mount.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was a good day for everybody,\xe2\x80\x9d he said with a laugh. \xe2\x80\x9cIt\xe2\x80\x99s been a while since I\xe2\x80\x99ve been in contention here. Tomorrow will be interesting.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Compared to most of the field, who generally attacked a rain-softened golf course and surged up the leaderboard in the early going on Saturday, Woods was the slow starter in the third round. His fans shadowed him from shot to shot, but they were subdued, especially after Woods bogeyed the fifth hole and dropped several strokes behind Tony Finau, who also finished Saturday at 11 under.'
b'On the walk from the fifth green to the sixth tee, Woods talked to himself. He saw the low scores on the leaderboard. After his round, he noted that even some of the amateurs in the field were four or five under for the day.'
b'That got his attention.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cThe golf course is certainly gettable,\xe2\x80\x9d Woods said.'
b'But instead of becoming overly aggressive, he remembered where he was. This was Augusta National, which rarely rewards the brash.'
b'He said to himself, \xe2\x80\x9cJust be patient; let the round build.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'His tee shot to the par-3 sixth green stopped 12 feet from the hole, and Woods curled in the tricky downhill birdie putt with a deft left-to-right break. Another birdie followed on the seventh hole, and at the par-5 eighth, his second shot stopped 11 feet from the hole. His eagle attempt skidded just past it.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIt was the only putt I missed all day,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cBut it was a good putt.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Woods was now eight under par for the tournament and a stroke off the lead. The galleries stalked him into Amen Corner, where he laid up before Rae\xe2\x80\x99s Creek but pitched to 6 feet and made that birdie putt, too.'
b'The par 5s have always been where Woods has won and lost Masters championships. The 13th hole is his favorite, and in 22 Masters appearances, he is 52 under par there. The next most generous hole for Woods has been the par-5 15th. On Saturday, it was at there that his round went from promising to memorable.'
b'His second shot bounded over the green, but Woods later said that was a calculation, not a mistake.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cIf you\xe2\x80\x99re going to miss, that\xe2\x80\x99s the place to miss,\xe2\x80\x9d he said. \xe2\x80\x9cI practice from that spot quite a bit in practice rounds. It was a simple chip.\xe2\x80\x9d'
b'Perhaps, but from just off the green, Woods had to deftly pitch his ball up a mound in the middle of the green and then let it trundle toward the front \xe2\x80\x94 with the right speed. But that\xe2\x80\x99s what he did. When he converted the 18-inch birdie putt, Woods was briefly tied for the lead with Molinari.'
b'The viewing spaces were packed at the par-3 16th when Woods, after an extended wait on the tee as he took eight practice swings, lofted a tee shot that bounced just left of the flagstick and skipped to a stop 5 feet away.'
b'\xe2\x80\x9cI took a little time but got the right wind there at 16 and hit it right where I wanted,\xe2\x80\x9d Woods said later.'
b'It produced his final birdie of the day and another ovation that would not be his last.'
b'Woods played the final two holes cautiously, or, more likely, prudently.'
b'And then he was walking across the 18th green, playing to a euphoric crowd that wanted more, and knew there was more to come.'

b'By The Associated Press'
b'HILTON HEAD ISLAND, S.C. \xe2\x80\x94 Francesco Molinari feels worn out after collapsing on the final nine at the Masters last week and is looking to conjure up the mental energy to compete at the RBC Heritage.'
b'Molinari, the reigning British Open champion, carried a two-stroke lead with seven holes left before a pair of uncharacteristic mistakes. He landed shots in the water on the 12th and 15th holes for two double-bogeys at Augusta National that dropped him from contention into a tie for fifth, two shots behind winner Tiger Woods.'
b' Molinari acknowledged Wednesday that he is still seeking the spark to move past last Sunday and get him going at Harbour Town Golf Links.'
b'"You try," he said. "You\'re never quite sure how long that\'s going to take."'
b"Molinari won't have long if he plans to contend. He faces another stacked field that includes Masters' runner ups and Dustin Johnson and Xander Schauffele, along with Webb Simpson, who finished tied with Molinari."
b'In all, 11 of the top 30 players in the world, led by No. 1 Johnson, will tee it up to start Thursday.'
b'Woods, who has only played in one RBC Heritage in 1999, is off this week.'
b'Molinari said his mistakes were straightforward and easy enough to diagnose with a bad swing on the par-3 12th and a bad choice on the part-5 15th.'
b'"But more than that, my concern is just having the mental energies to perform this week and be competitive against a really strong field. That will be the challenge for me," he said.'
b" Molinari, 36, has been a revelation, especially in majors, the last two seasons. He's posted four top six finishes, including his British Open win at Carnoustie last July, over his past six major tournaments after never finishing better than ninth in his first 32 such appearances."
b'Johnson was pleased with his performance at Augusta, despite missing a birdie putt on the 72nd hole that might have tied him with Woods.'
b'"Obviously, one stroke, definitely could\'ve found that somewhere," Johnson said. "But all in all, it was a good week and I played well when I needed to."'
b"Johnson, a South Carolina native, returned to Harbour Town last year for the first time in almost a decade and finished tied for 16th, his best RBC Heritage showing in three appearances. The speculation on Johnson's extended absence are similar to theories about why Woods does not play here \xe2\x80\x94 tight, unforgiving fairways where positioning shots is as important as bombing them a long way."
b'"If I\'m playing well, I enjoy any golf course," Johnson countered. "If I\'m hitting the ball where I want to, no matter what type of course it is, I like it. This is the kind of golf I grew up playing. It\'s something I\'m used to. Last year, I had some success and I\'m looking to have some more success this year."'
b'Simpson, too, believes his strong play at the Masters can continue this week. One of his two top-five career finishes at Harbour Town came last year.'
b'"I know what to do around this golf course," he said. "It\'s kind of a quirky, tricky golf course, but I always love being here."'
b"Despite last week's events, Molinari said he carries much more confidence into all his tournaments these days. His three PGA Tour victories have all come since last July, including a win last month at the Arnold Palmer Invitational."
b'"I\'ve never been a guy who showed up on tour and started winning straight away," Molinari said. "Definitely the last few steps have been more mental rather than technical or anything else."'
b'Molinari, ranked seventh in the world, will put that to the test when this tournament ends with three weeks off before returning to action at the PGA Championship at Bethpage Black in New York. Molinari backed up his British Open win with a sixth at the PGA last August and is anxious for the next one.'
b'"I\'ll analyze with a colder mind what happened (at the Masters) and just move forward toward Bethpage," Molinari said.'
